Requests Anhui Provincial Government to Protect Cocoon Merchants

Huang Yunchen, chairman of the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Silk Cocoon General Guild, yesterday submitted a memorial to Chairman Chen of the Anhui Provincial Government, requesting additional military police to protect the cocoon market, stating: "Memorial for the protection of the cocoon market, advance preparations with reference to previous years' memoranda, respectfully requesting investigation and approval, ordering all subordinates to strictly defend and protect, in order to secure agricultural commerce. Investigate that every new cocoon crop is successively opened to the market during the Xiaoman solar term. Every year, the general guild drafts and presents protection measures, which are presented to the National Government, distributed to all provinces and regions, and circulated for protection, and printed protection measures are presented to Your Excellency for distribution to all cocoon-producing areas for investigation and handling, so as to provide thorough protection, and we are deeply grateful. The cocoon market is approaching this year, and the bandits in various parts of Anhui Province have not been completely cleared. With the new cocoons coming to market, precautions should be complete, and the cocoon trading locations are mostly in rural towns. Farmers bring cocoons to the exchanges, and cocoon merchants bring silver to buy cocoons. The roads and the locations of the exchanges must have substantial protection to avoid fear and seek safety. The general guild has a responsibility to prepare in advance, detailing all aspects that require protection, such as the transport of silver and the transfer of cocoon bales, with reference to past practices and noting the dates. We respectfully request Your Excellency to preside over the matter and earnestly distribute it to all cocoon-producing counties, quickly ordering all stationed regiments and all county water and land public security bureaus to protect and implement it in accordance with the regulations. In addition to printing and distributing the detailed measures, we are sending one hundred additional copies to Your Excellency's government for distribution to all cocoon-producing counties and the military police chiefs responsible for protection for investigation and implementation. All the reasons for the advance petition for protection of the cocoon market, with the attached measures, are hereby submitted. May we be granted investigation and implementation, and may the instructions be followed, for the public good. Respectfully presented."

Zhejiang Cocoon Industry Association 100

Request for Allocation of Construction Bonds

Telegram to the Zhejiang Provincial Finance and Construction Bureaus

The United Association of Zhejiang Provincial Cocoon Industry Guilds in this city yesterday sent a telegram to the Zhejiang Provincial Finance and Construction Bureaus, requesting the allocation of construction bonds to relieve the cocoon industry crisis. The text reads:

To the Zhejiang Finance Bureau: Respected Director of the Zhejiang Finance Bureau, since the sales of Chinese silk to Europe have been sluggish, the cocoon industry has been affected accordingly. No one is renting cocoon exchanges, and silk factories are watching the market before purchasing cocoons. There are no fewer than a thousand cocoon exchanges in Zhejiang Province. The time for new cocoons to enter the market is only ten days away, but less than one-tenth of those preparing to obtain licenses and operate are ready. Cocoon exchanges are responsible for managing cocoons, purchasing farmers' produce, and raw silk materials, bearing the mission of production, sales, supply, and demand. The responsibility is extremely heavy. If relief is not arranged quickly, it will not be a matter of great importance to the individual cocoon exchanges but will have a significant impact on the rural economy. The reason for the decline is that the losses last year were huge, and businesses are unable to continue operating. The association has repeatedly convened meetings of the industry to discuss relief methods. It is the consensus that only by requesting assistance from the government and providing large loans can the situation be maintained. In addition to telegraphing the Construction Bureau to forward the request to the Ministry of Industry to allocate 1.5 million yuan from the 2 million yuan of silk industry bonds for the improvement of sericulture, we are sincerely afraid that it will be too slow to be effective. Moreover, according to statistics from all cocoon exchanges in the province, the amount is still insufficient. Therefore, we propose consulting with the Construction Bureau to temporarily approve the allocation of 2 million yuan from the 7 million yuan of unsold construction bonds in the province for the relief of the cocoon industry. The method is to issue them to the county governments of each county, which will then transfer them to local banks or money shops, allowing cocoon merchants to seek guarantees for borrowing. They will be required to repay within a short period of time. In this transition, uselessness can be transformed into usefulness. The government will not suffer any loss, while the people will benefit greatly. Moreover, using it for the construction of industry in the name of construction is more appropriate than other uses. At this time of the cocoon industry crisis, which is on the verge of collapse, we also ask you to promptly and clearly announce the exemptions from the regular and additional donations levied on dried cocoons, and to instruct the counties not to establish other items of collection. If any similar cocoon donations are collected again, merchants and people will clearly understand the government's active assistance and relief, encourage themselves to continue working, and our cocoon industry may still have a day of revitalization. The situation is urgent, and we respectfully ask you to consider and implement it.

Page 10

For your consideration, furthermore, cocoon merchants from various regions are gathering in Shanghai to negotiate cocoon sales and lease matters. For the convenience of handling affairs, an office has been established in Shanghai, which is hereby reported together. The Preparatory Committee of the United Association of Zhejiang Provincial Cocoon Industry Guilds bows respectfully.

To the Zhejiang Construction Bureau: Respected Director Shi of the Zhejiang Construction Bureau, the silkworm season has arrived early, and the cocoon market is about to open. There are no fewer than a thousand cocoon exchanges in the province, but less than one-tenth have decided to operate. On the 3rd of this month, the association held its fourth preparatory meeting. According to the reports of the representatives of the various guilds present, out of 107 cocoon exchanges in Jiaxing County, less than 10 have decided to operate. Out of 58 in Haiyan, only 4 have decided to operate. Out of 28 in Pinghu, only 7 have decided to operate. The reports from the counties of Hangzhou, Shaoxing, and Huzhou are mostly the same. The decline of the cocoon industry has reached an extreme state. If relief is not sought quickly, not only will all cocoon exchanges go bankrupt, but rural households will have difficulty selling their cocoons, and many will become moths and rot, turning usefulness into uselessness, affecting cocoon production to a great extent. The livelihood of farmers in the province, in addition to agricultural income, depends largely on silkworm farming. Rent and taxes, food and clothing, all depend on it. Once livelihoods are sharply reduced, the people of Zhejiang, who have suffered from disasters and famines for a long time, how can they bear this? Upon investigation, the 2 million yuan in the Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Industry Bonds for the improvement of sericulture is not an immediate need. We earnestly request that you consider the close relationship between the interests of the cocoon industry and the silkworm farmers and approve the forwarding of a request to the Ministry of Industry to allocate 1.5 million yuan as a measure to shift from slow to urgent, and temporarily allocate it for the relief of the Zhejiang cocoon industry. Once approved, please issue it to the county governments of each county and temporarily issue it to local banks or money shops, allowing the cocoon exchanges to seek guarantees for borrowing to facilitate turnover. Directly, it is to relieve the cocoon industry; indirectly, it is to relieve the farmers. In addition to recommending representatives Chu Huiseng, Xu Xingbin, and Huang Weisang to go to the province to petition and discuss the methods in person, we first telegraph this request. We respectfully ask you to consider and implement it. It will be a great favor. Furthermore, cocoon merchants from various regions are gathering in Shanghai to negotiate cocoon sales and lease matters. For the convenience of handling affairs, an office has been established in Shanghai, which is hereby reported together. The Preparatory Committee of the United Association of Zhejiang Provincial Cocoon Industry Guilds bows respectfully.

Sand and Gravel Industry 101

Petition to Abolish the Production Tax

According to the Guomin News Agency, the Sand and Gravel Industry Guild in this city, unable to bear the heavy production tax, has submitted a petition to the authorities, which reads: Submitting a petition for the abolition of arbitrarily established names and the imposition of exorbitant taxes, to alleviate the people's difficulties and alleviate the merchants' hardships. The sand and mud sold by the guild are essentially taking waste materials and benefiting the people's livelihood, and can also dredge rivers and waterways. The selling price is two yuan per ton, which is not a material value but a substitute for labor costs. The firms that fill in the forms and sell them also deduct a commission of only one jiao per ton. Therefore, it has been the practice for decades that the government has been generous and has not levied taxes. Unexpectedly, at this time of tax reduction, our industry is being levied a heavy tax, reaching more than 50%, exceeding the business tax by more than 200 times. Arbitrarily established names such as management fees and production taxes are used to set up branch checkpoints, threatening and extorting donations, which are trapping the common people and infringing on commerce. After the National Government abolished the likin tax and replaced it with a business tax, it repeatedly issued circular telegrams to the whole country, announcing that no other exorbitant taxes should be collected in addition to the business tax, to eliminate accumulated abuses and benefit the people. Moreover, the sand and gravel we collect has already been paid for the production price to the local authorities, and donations have been made for education and police expenses. Furthermore, removing sand and mud can eliminate the siltation of the river channels, so there is no need for management, and the price cannot be repeatedly collected. This is obviously a false claim by unscrupulous merchants to deceive and profit. If this trend is started, others will follow suit, which will have a significant impact on commerce. After celebrating the abolition of the likin tax, we are again suffering from exorbitant taxes. If the industry suffers such a heavy burden, the livelihoods of 40,000 to 50,000 people in the city who rely on it will be in a desperate situation. Therefore, we urgently submit this petition, requesting that the government approve the abolition of this exorbitant tax to alleviate the people's difficulties and alleviate the merchants' hardships. It will be a public benefit. Respectfully submitted.

Ministry Promulgated 102

Regulations for the Transportation of Dangerous Goods by the Military

Since the tragic accident of the Daji Steamer of the Dada Company, it has aroused the attention of the whole country. The Shanghai Shipping Guild has recently received instructions from the Ministry of Communications to formulate regulations for soldiers carrying gunpowder, explosives, and other items in the future to prevent such incidents. The details are as follows:

Instructions: To Whom It May Concern, regarding the Ministry of Communications' Order No. 1670, approved by the Ministry of Military Affairs' consultation, approved by the Ministry of Finance's Order No. 18781, approved by the Customs Administration's presentation, according to the Chief Commissioner of Customs' presentation, according to the Commissioner of the Jianghai Customs' report, the Dada Company's Daji Steamer caught fire and was burned on the evening of March 11 in the Dashudun area of the Yangtze River due to the explosion of gunpowder on board. The Customs' special patrol boat and the Dahe Steamer rushed to the rescue, rescuing a total of 191 people and transporting them to Shanghai. The cause of the ship's accident and the observations are respectfully submitted to you. The ship was heading to Tongzhou and Yangzhou on March 10. When it left Shanghai, it carried a total of 537 passengers. When the ship arrived in Tongzhou, a large number of passengers disembarked. At that time, there were some passengers, and 41 soldiers carrying guns, ammunition, and hand grenades boarded the ship from Tongzhou. Therefore, when the ship left Tongzhou, the total number of passengers, including soldiers, was 356. The cause of the accident was that the soldiers did not place the ammunition they were carrying in a safe place, and it was reported that some gunpowder was not properly placed, so when the remnants of cigarettes were thrown and approached the ammunition, a tragedy occurred. The above-mentioned circumstances of the case are deeply hoped that all parties will pay attention to. The military's carrying of dangerous goods on passenger ships not only disregards the safety of passengers, but also ignores the danger to themselves, and arbitrarily places the explosives they carry on the ship. Although the crew members warned them, they ignored them. This situation is known to all and is prone to danger. Therefore, according to the Commissioner of Customs' observation, the dispatch of troops by ship is a constant occurrence, but there must be regulations for the storage of dangerous goods by the military, which must be strictly observed. In the future, the troops attached to passenger ships will not have similar tragedies. The cause of the Daji Steamer's accident and the reasons for the observations are in line with the Port Captain's report on the Daji Steamer and the report of the surveyor who previously inspected the ship. They are submitted together for review. The details of the report are factual, and the attached reports are attached together. The details are prepared and submitted for review, and forwarded to the Ministry of Military Affairs to order the military officers in charge to pay close attention to the dangerous goods such as explosives carried by the troops in the future when they are dispatched and attached to passenger ships, so as to avoid similar tragedies and ensure safety and maintain the shipping industry. Two attached reports are attached. According to this, the cause of the tragic accident of the Daji Steamer was that the soldiers on board did not place the ammunition they were carrying in a safe place, and when they encountered the remnants of cigarettes, they caused a very serious disaster. If the military does not strictly establish regulations for compliance when traveling on merchant ships in the future, it will not only endanger the shipping industry, but also greatly affect military discipline. Now, in order to prevent future troubles, we must take precautions. It is proposed that your ministry formulate detailed regulations in the regulations and circulate them to all military agencies for compliance in order to maintain the shipping industry and discipline the military administration. According to the report, a copy of the report is enclosed and sent to your ministry for investigation and implementation. It is hoped that you will reply. Two attached reports are attached. According to this, it is now approved that the Ministry has drafted the Regulations for the Transportation of Dangerous Goods by the Military on Ships and will be promulgated and implemented on May 1. In addition to presenting and notifying separately, a copy of the regulations is enclosed and sent to you for investigation and compliance. This order and other matters are attached with a copy of the Regulations for the Transportation of Dangerous Goods by the Military on Ships. According to this, the attached documents are recorded and printed, and a letter is sent to you for your information.

Regulations: Regulations for the Transportation of Dangerous Goods by the Military on Ships, Article 1: Accidents often occur due to improper handling of the transportation of dangerous goods by the military on ships. In order to prevent such incidents, these regulations are specifically formulated for compliance. Dangerous goods in these regulations refer to various gunpowder, bullets, artillery shells, bombs, toxic gases, and various incendiary devices. Article 2: Before transporting dangerous goods on board, the highest director of the transportation unit (agency) shall appoint a special escort commissioner to carry a military transportation passport or certificate, which shall be verified by the shipowner to designate a suitable cabin before loading. Article 3: No passengers are allowed to enter the cargo hold where dangerous goods are stored, except for crew members, to avoid accidents. Article 4: The cargo hold for loading dangerous goods shall not be close to the engine room and kitchen to avoid vibration and explosion. Article 5: Dangerous goods of different properties shall not be loaded in the same cabin, and all easily flammable or explosive items shall not be approached, and shall be isolated from ordinary commercial goods. Article 6: The loading and unloading of dangerous goods must be stable, safe, and completed quickly, and there shall be no throwing, rolling, or other such incidents. Article 7: The cabin door for storing dangerous goods shall be locked day and night, and the escort commissioner shall inspect the surrounding area outside the door from time to time, and soldiers shall be assigned to guard in shifts to prevent negligence. Article 8: Escort officers and soldiers are not allowed to smoke, drink, or cause trouble. The soldiers on guard are not allowed to sit or lie down at will or leave their posts without authorization. Article 9: The escort officers and soldiers shall be subject to the crew's dispatch for opening and stopping the ship, and shall not interfere arbitrarily, and shall not insult the crew. Article 10: If the escort officers and soldiers have any circumstances of contracting passengers and carrying goods in addition to the designated number of people and items, and violate the provisions of these regulations, the shipowner may report to the nearest highest military agency for disposal before reporting to the Ministry of Military Affairs for review. Article 11: If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, they may be submitted for revision. Article 12: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Location for the Collection of Business Tax on Egg Factories 103

Request for Determination by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing yesterday, stating: Respected Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, on the 7th of this month, we received a letter from the Egg Factory Guild in this city, stating that our members are purely Chinese-funded and purchase fresh eggs in egg-producing areas in the interior, such as Jiangsu, Anhui, Shandong, Henan, Hubei, and other provinces, and set up factories locally to produce dried and wet egg yolks, which are transported to Shanghai and sold by Shanghai branches to foreign firms for export. The so-called branches are the exclusive sales agencies set up by various factories in the interior, or one factory has one branch, or two or three factories jointly set up one branch. These egg yolks and egg whites are not sold domestically and rely entirely on European and American countries for the final outlet. Therefore, in terms of inland factories, they only buy but do not sell, and in terms of Shanghai branches, they only sell but do not buy. Only when the factory and the branch are combined can a business be formed. Now, in order to maintain the tax revenue after the abolition of the likin tax, the government will implement business taxes as compensation. Upon investigation, the business tax regulations of each province do not include the name of the egg yolk and egg white manufacturing industry. Although the draft business tax rate proposed by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Finance lists the egg yolk and egg white industry in the manufacturing industry tax rate table, taxing it at 5/1000 of the capital amount, none of our members have set up factories for manufacturing within the Shanghai municipal area. The branches set up are only a few income-generating, and there is no capital to speak of. Then, in the future, where will the business tax of our members be collected, either at the factory or at the Shanghai branch? If it is collected at the factory, what will be the basis for the tax rate in each province? These two points are questionable. Furthermore, the business nature of our members is entirely foreign trade. Recently, it has been affected by the United States' high profile of increasing import taxes, and the future of the business is precarious. In order to encourage foreign trade, the government's original intention is to maintain the national industry. The business tax rate for the egg yolk and egg white industry should be particularly low to show consideration and encouragement. We dare to ask your association to telegraph the Ministry of Finance for a prompt and clear explanation of the above two points and to specify a unified business tax rate for the egg yolk and egg white industry in each province so that we can follow it. Upon investigation, the industry sets up factories in the interior, but the transaction takes place in the Shanghai market. It must cross two administrative regions to complete the buying and selling activities. It is different from the business operations of the head office and branch. Then, should this business tax be collected at the location where the factory is set up or at the location where the transaction takes place? If the Ministry does not determine the method, disputes will inevitably arise between government offices, causing merchants to bear the burden repeatedly. We should truthfully telegraph your Ministry for review and give a discretionary method so that there will be compliance. As for the proposal of the industry to unify the business tax rate for the egg yolk and egg white manufacturing industry in each province, according to the regulations of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, the tax rate for the manufacturing industry is stipulated to be from 2/1000 to 24/1000 of the capital amount. The general regulations in Anhui Province are within 20/1000. How will the egg yolk and egg white manufacturing industry be regulated in the future? It is still difficult to speculate. The industry's statement that the business is in danger due to the recent increase in import tariffs in the United States is a factual situation. All provinces should consult with the Ministry and the current draft proposal of the city to determine a moderate tax rate so that each province may not exceed it, which may be enough to save it slightly. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce respectfully bows.

Continued Report on the Chaoyang Disaster in Rehe 106

Report on the Proceeds of the Jisheng Association

The China Jisheng Association previously reported on the tragic disaster in Chaoyang County, Rehe. The association and General Zhu Ziqiao jointly organized emergency relief, each allocating 10,000 yuan for relief, which has been recorded in previous reports. Now, we have received a detailed report from Mr. Yu Guisheng, the director of relief in the Tianjin office of the association, which stated that according to a friend from Chaoyang, the entire territory of Chaoyang is mountainous and watery. Last year, in addition to the flood disaster, there were also drought, frost, and hail disasters. The autumn harvest was disappointing, and people's food was extremely difficult. No one was hired to work, and there were many unemployed in both the industrial and commercial sectors. When one person loses their job, their parents, wives, and children are all suffering from hunger and cold. If no other solution is found, they will all die. Therefore, the elderly and the young went to the Northeast provinces to seek a living. They continued to beg for food along the way. The entire area was a disaster area, and they could not get enough to eat all day long. From Chaoyang to Jinzhou, it takes more than 20 days, and some even commit suicide halfway. Some die of hunger, some sell their children, and some husbands see their wives commit suicide and die, and then kill the children they carry with them and die together. All kinds of tragic situations are hard to describe. At present, there are many bandits in Chaoyang, most of whom are forced by hunger and cold, gathering a large number of victims and forcibly feeding large households. It has also been seen repeatedly. Now there are more than 2,000 people gathered here, requesting to go east to escape the famine. They are in a very embarrassing situation and urgently need help.

The China Moral Society and the Jisheng Association jointly organized relief in Jiangxi, which has been recorded in the newspapers. An Incident Regarding the Incense Pilgrimage at Jing'an Temple 108

A Petition and Appeal from Stallholders

Regarding the Bureau of Public Works' announcement restricting the setting up of stalls for this year's Buddha's Birthday at the Jing'an Temple in West Shanghai, stallholders have initiated a temporary Stallholders' Union. They have publicly elected more than ten people, including Xi Yongxin, Li Zhaolian, and Jiang Peiyun, as committee members and hired lawyer Chen Ruilin as an advisor. They have jointly petitioned the Bureau of Public Works, urging them to retract their decision, and have appealed to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, and others. The text of their petition is recorded as follows:

To the Bureau of Public Works: A petition to earnestly request the retraction of the restrictive order on setting up stalls for Buddha's Birthday at Jing'an Temple in order to maintain the livelihood of ordinary people. We, the small merchants, read in the Shenbao newspaper on April 26th that Your Bureau has decided to restrict stall locations for this year's Buddha's Birthday festival at Jing'an Temple in Shanghai. Upon hearing this, we were shocked and terrified. The practice of setting up stalls for Buddha's Birthday at Jing'an Temple has a long history of over a thousand years. Every year, the small merchants set up stalls for about ten days during Buddha's Birthday to sell local products and miscellaneous goods manufactured throughout the year in the city, earning meager profits to sustain their livelihoods for the year. In recent years, the population of the concessions has increased, and the area for stalls should have been expanded. However, Your Bureau, citing traffic concerns, has instead proposed restrictions, prohibiting stalls around Jing'an Temple and in front of shops. Only scattered, isolated sections are designated, separated on all sides and unable to connect. Business is bound to plummet. We believe that this restriction is tantamount to strict prohibition, eliminating a long-standing custom. The small merchants have already been guarding their stall locations for over a month and are now affected by this, unable to set up stalls, thus cutting off the livelihood of the poor. Furthermore, Jing'an Temple had a land lease contract with Your Bureau in 1899, which stipulated that stalls were permitted to be set up freely during Buddha's Birthday. The roads have been widened in recent years, and stalls used to be set up in the middle of the roads, but in recent years, they have been set up on the small roads on both sides, so they do not obstruct traffic. It is only that there are many pilgrims and tourists, and vehicles cannot travel at high speed. As for setting up stalls in front of shops, businesses have actually increased as a result, so shopkeepers have never opposed it. This stall setup is beneficial to society, the people's livelihood, and local commerce. Considering that Your Bureau has always been dedicated to helping ordinary people and benefiting society, we jointly and earnestly request Your Bureau to retract the restrictive order on setting up stalls, preserve the custom of previous years, and maintain the livelihood of over a thousand stallholders. This would be a great act of benevolence. Respectfully submitted to the Director-General of the Board of Directors of the Bureau of Public Works.

To the Bureau of Social Affairs: A petition to appeal for efforts to persuade the Bureau of Public Works to retract the restriction on setting up stalls for Buddha's Birthday at Jing'an Temple in order to maintain the livelihood of ordinary people. We, the small merchants, read in the newspaper that the Bureau of Public Works is restricting the setting up of stalls and the sale of domestic goods at this year's Buddha's Birthday festival at Jing'an Temple in West Shanghai. Upon hearing this, we were deeply shocked. The setting up of stalls has been a custom for thousands of years, exclusively selling domestic goods and local products. Every year, the small merchants take advantage of this Buddha's Birthday opportunity to set up stalls for about ten days to sell off all the goods they have made throughout the year to sustain their livelihoods for the year. Now, the Bureau of Public Works, citing traffic obstruction as a pretext, has initiated a strict restriction, prohibiting stalls on the roads near Jing'an Temple and in front of shops. Only a small number of isolated sections in remote areas are permitted, separated on all sides and unable to connect. Business is hopeless. Moreover, the stallholders have been braving the elements and guarding their old stall locations for over a month, and now they are affected by this, unable to set up stalls, thus cutting off the livelihood of us ordinary people. Furthermore, Jing'an Temple had a land lease contract with the Bureau of Public Works in 1899, which stipulated that stalls were permitted to be set up freely during Buddha's Birthday. The roads around Jing'an Temple have all been widened, and stalls that used to be set up in the middle of the roads have recently been moved to the small roads on both sides, so there is absolutely no reason to obstruct traffic. It is only that there are many pilgrims and tourists, and many vehicles, so only cars cannot travel at high speed. All the shops have increased their business because of the stalls over the years, and we have never heard of any opposition to the stalls. This stall setup is truly a commercial arena for promoting domestic goods, beneficial to society and the people's livelihood, and not insignificant. Therefore, we appeal to Your Bureau to uphold justice, grant relief, and assist in efforts to persuade in order to promote domestic goods and maintain the livelihoods of thousands of ordinary people. We would be deeply grateful. (The petitions to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Chinese Ratepayers' Association are the same and are omitted.)

Sea Bandits Rob Fishing Boats

Five Patrol Boats Go to Suppress

Postponement of Direct Collection of Slaughter Tax 112

The slaughter tax on fresh pork in this city has been contracted to meat merchants, who then collect it from various shops. The collection method does not follow the regulations of paying 39 cents per pig. Instead, it is collected according to the size of each meat merchant's business, ranging from four or five yuan per shop per month to seven or eight yuan, ten or more yuan, or twenty or more yuan. Currently, the Finance Bureau, in order to reorganize taxes and duties, and because the contract period for the contractors has expired, has decided to directly collect from each shop starting on May 1st. Regardless of the number of pigs slaughtered, tax tickets must be purchased according to the regulations. However, the meat merchants believe that this method is not only troublesome procedurally but also requires more taxes to be paid. For example, if a shop usually slaughters one pig per day, totaling thirty pigs per month, paying 39 cents per pig according to the regulations would require paying 11 yuan and 70 cents. However, under the contractor system, paying five or six yuan was sufficient. Larger shops slaughter three or four pigs or five or six pigs per day, and the tax they pay is only ten or more yuan or twenty or more yuan. Therefore, the shops are observing and unwilling to purchase tax tickets for the direct collection of taxes by the Finance Bureau. The Finance Bureau's implementation of the collection yesterday resulted in slaughtered white pigs from various workshops not being allowed to be sent out without tax tickets. On the same day, representatives of the industry, Rong Qianchu, Shen Xie, Ye Xiangxian, and Huang Yexin, went to the Municipal Government to request a postponement of the direct collection. The Municipal Government agreed to postpone it for one week, to be implemented on the 15th, and instructed the representatives to persuade their colleagues. It is also heard that the meat merchants have now sent representatives to the capital to petition and have scheduled a meeting at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce on the 14th to discuss the matter.

Rice Merchants Attempt to Manipulate Rice Prices Again 113

Fortunately, the Authorities Stopped it in Time

Since the spring of this year, rice prices in Shanghai have been stable, with no significant fluctuations. Recently, there were rumors that Northern gangs were shipping rice, and manipulators, hearing this, scrambled to hoard rice, believing that prices would inevitably rise after the Northern gangs shipped rice, and they could make huge profits by selling it. Therefore, prices have been rising daily in recent weeks. Northern Dingbai rice has now risen to 13 yuan and 45 cents, while Southern Sutong white rice initially opened at 10 yuan, 34 cents, but rose to 11 yuan and 70 cents yesterday. This was discovered by the authorities, who, believing that the rice price increase was related to the people's livelihood at a time when the new crop was not yet available, ordered the rice industry not to raise prices and investigated whether there were any export activities. The market has gradually stabilized in the past two days.

The Lu Shaotang Case 115

The Leader of the Kidnappers Was Arrested in Beiping

A Dispute Arises on a Tram 116

The Stealing Chicken Bridge Car Stopped for Twenty Minutes

The French-operated Route 5 tram, which runs between the West Gate and the North Station, stopped at Stealing Chicken Bridge on Zhejiang Road at about 9 p.m. last night. Three passengers wanted to board the tram to go north. The driver refused to open the door, saying that there were too many passengers on the tram. The passengers insisted on boarding, leading to arguments. The two sides almost came to blows. A crowd gathered to watch, and the driver stopped moving forward. The stalemate lasted for twenty minutes. The police on duty brought both parties to the police station to resolve the matter. Several passengers on the tram, willing to testify, also went along. However, when Route 5 stopped, other trams, such as Route 7, Route 6, and Route 3, were unable to proceed, blocking the road and disrupting traffic. It is said that the three passengers who wanted to board Route 5 were special police officers from the police station.

Record of the Preparatory Meeting for the Memorial Service for Zhang Shisheng 117

Mr. Zhang Shisheng of Haimen devoted himself to the cause of Chinese medicine for nearly thirty years. Unfortunately, he died of illness in his hometown in the third month of the lunar calendar. The medical communities across the country were shocked and mourned his passing. Now, Zhang's old friends Ding Zhongying, Zhang Meian, Shen Tingdong, Bao Shisheng, and others have initiated a memorial service. The first preparatory meeting was convened yesterday at the National Medical Association. More than twenty people attended, including Ding Zhongying, Zhang Meian, Shen Tingdong, Bao Shisheng, Chen Cunren, Huang Baozhong, Tang Liangchen, Jiang Wenfang, Huang Cuocai, Fan Fayuan, Yan Cangshan, Fu Yongyan, and Chen Xusheng. Zhang Meian was publicly elected as chairman. First, Zhang Junzhuan, son of Zhang Shisheng, reported on his father's illness and last words. Then, the memorial service plan was discussed and the following resolutions were made: (1) Regarding the determination of the name of the memorial service, it was resolved to name it "The Memorial Service for Mr. Zhang Shisheng, Who Devoted Himself to the Cause of Chinese Medicine." (2) Regarding the scope of the organization of the memorial service, it was resolved that in addition to individuals participating as initiators, organizations such as the National Medical Association, the Shanghai National Medical Association, the National Pharmaceutical Industry Association, and various medical schools should all join as initiators and jointly mourn. Zhang Meian, Ding Zhongying, Jiang Wenfang, Bao Shisheng, Fu Yongyan, Huang Baozhong, Yan Cangshan, and Shen Tingdong were appointed to be responsible for the preparation. (3) The expenses of the memorial service and the preparatory office will be borne by the initiators. (4) The preparatory office will be located at Room 14, 2nd Floor, Yizhong Real Estate Company, No. 274 Zhejiang Road, inside the Shanghai National Medical Association. (5) The memorial date is scheduled for June 16th of the Gregorian calendar, and the location will be borrowed from the Ningbo Fellow Association. (6) The preparatory office will notify medical groups in other cities to join the public memorial. (7) Zhang Meian was appointed to edit the special memorial publication. (8) A public notice will be published in the newspaper in the name of the preparatory office to inform the public. (9) It was decided to hold preparatory meetings every Saturday.

Liu Ziming 118

Implicated by the Name "Little Leper Head"

The Main Culprit in a Murder Case Also Has This Name

He Was Released After a Witness Testified

Wang A'da, a native of Ningbo, was shot and injured on February 19th of last year near the Deyilou Tea House on Seward Road. Wang Wanfu, Tang Xingfa, Tong Xingsheng, and others were arrested at the time and sentenced by the court to imprisonment. However, the main culprit, "Little Leper Head," escaped. Now, according to the Hongkou Police Station, Liu Ziming, a native of Ningbo residing at No. 2332 Zhaofeng Road, nicknamed "Little Leper Head," may be the main culprit in the case. He was arrested and sent to the Special District Local Court for interrogation. The magistrate Xiao brought him in for interrogation the other day. The police also brought in Wang Wanfu and others, who were imprisoned in the West Prison, for questioning. The victim, Wang A'da, also appeared in court and described the circumstances of the assassination. After carefully identifying Liu Ziming, he solemnly stated that the "Little Leper Head" who committed the crime was short and not as burly as the defendant, and there must be another person. He said that he could still identify the "Little Leper Head" if he was arrested. Wang Wanfu and others also testified that the defendant was not present. The defendant hired a lawyer to clarify that he had been wrongly arrested and requested his release. Magistrate Xiao ruled that according to the testimony of all parties, the defendant was indeed not related to the case and immediately ordered his acquittal. The police lawyer also stated that he had no objection to the verdict. The magistrate then ordered his immediate release.

A Young Man Entices a Butcher's Wife to Elopes 119

Xu Xinzhang, a butcher from Ningbo residing at No. 300 Benzai Lane, Yuezhou Road, is already over forty years old, while his wife, Jin, is only nineteen years old. The mismatch in their ages made her susceptible to love affairs, so she had an affair with a young man named Fan Fuxue. This was discovered in April of this year. However, Xu loved his wife deeply and did not want her to suffer, so he ordered Fan to write a confession, stipulating three rules that he should not have similar actions in the future, thinking that he had taken extreme precautions and there would be no further problems. However, the connection was not severed, and they continued as before, only more discreetly. Therefore, she felt constrained. The other day, Fan took advantage of Xu's absence to entice her to elope. They were about to disappear, but Xu's brother saw them and arrested them on behalf of his brother and called the police. They were detained in the Third Precinct, Fifth Sub-station. Xu returned home and learned of the situation, becoming very angry and demanding an investigation at the police station. Yesterday, the case was transferred to the Local Court for interrogation.

A Big Fight Over Trying to Watch a Free Show 120

A Martial Arts Play at the Yangjiadu Dongxing Theater

The Yangjiadu Main Street in Pudong is densely populated with migrant residents. Previously, Chen Guoliang and others from Jiangbei opened a theater called the Dongxing Theater, hiring Huaiyang actors to perform Yangzhou opera, opening day and night, and doing good business. However, conflicts occasionally arose between the audience and the theater due to minor issues. Last year, the local police station ordered them to stop performing for several months due to an accident. Later, they were allowed to continue performing, but disputes still occurred from time to time. Unexpectedly, a major conflict broke out between the audience and the ticket seller at about 8 p.m. the other night. A few men had come to the theater pretending to be looking for someone, intending to watch the show for free. The ticket seller refused and spoke harshly to them. Suddenly, more than ten people rushed in from outside and fought with the ticket sellers. Teapots and teacups were smashed, and the theater was in chaos. The audience dispersed. Two ticket sellers, Yu Zaihou and Shi Xianzhu, were seriously injured and sent to a hospital in Puxi for treatment. When the conflict first broke out, the theater owner, Chen Guoliang, immediately reported it to the Third Precinct, First Sub-station, and the police officer on duty led a large group of police officers to the scene. The perpetrators Huang Xiaoerzi, Cao Xiaoyu, Huang Ruxiang, Wu Xiaobao, Wu Er, Zhang Youcai, Qin Daguozi, Ji Xiaoxizi, Chen Xiaowuzi, Li Alin, Zhang Xiaowuzi, and eleven others were arrested and taken to the police station. Later, another person shouted to those arrested in front of the police station, telling them not to confess to the assault. He was also arrested by the guards on duty. Under interrogation, he said his name was Yang (nicknamed Jiangbei Boss) and admitted to being the leader of the gang. After investigating the matter, the police chief Yang determined that the case was related to disturbing public order and ordered that they be sent to the Public Security Bureau for punishment.

A Country Woman Becomes Depraved After Coming to Shanghai 121

She Lives with a Paramour and Beats Her Husband

Zhao Bizhu from Gaoyou married Zhao Zhu, who is 28 years old. Both were farmers in their hometown. Zhao Zhu, unable to endure the hard work in the fields, told her husband that she wanted to come to Shanghai to work as a servant, so that she could save effort and make a profit. Her husband thought it was a good idea and sent her off at the riverbank, telling her to send news home often to ease his worries. Unexpectedly, more than a year passed without any news. He came to Shanghai to look for her a few days ago, staying at No. 2, Xinshali, Xixie Bridge in West Shanghai. He searched everywhere but could not find her. He had not seen her stay with any family among his fellow villagers. Unexpectedly, Zhao Zhu passed by the alley yesterday, and Zhao saw that she resembled his wife, so he followed her. Zhao Zhu was living with Zhou Jintang at No. 14 Fuxing Lane. She even denied that Zhao was her husband and drove him away with a stick. Zhao, in a panic, called the police, and Zhou and Zhao Zhu were arrested and taken to the Second Precinct Police Station, and then transferred to the Local Court for interrogation.

After Three Years Without News of Her Husband 122

Zhang Zhuxiuqing Requests a Divorce

Zhang Zhuxiuqing, a woman from Songjiang, recently hired a lawyer to sue her husband, Zhang Liansheng, in the Local Court for abandonment and desertion for three years, requesting a divorce. Zhao Zhenhai, the presiding judge, opened the court for trial yesterday morning. The defendant, Zhang Liansheng, could not be served because his address was unknown, so he did not appear in court. A specially appointed lawyer, Zhou Yu, appeared in court to defend him. According to Zhang Zhuxiuqing's statement, she is 30 years old, lives in Caojiadu, West Shanghai, and works in a yarn factory. Ten years ago, she married Zhang Liansheng in her hometown with the help of a matchmaker and had two sons, one ten years old and the other only four years old. Later, she came to Shanghai with her husband and rented a house in Caojiadu. Unexpectedly, her husband went out on his own in November 1927 and never returned. More than three years have passed since then, and his whereabouts are unknown. She searched everywhere but could not find him. She is a woman who supports herself by doing some women's work, but it is still not enough. She also has to raise two sons, which is difficult to maintain. (Question) Do you want to remarry? (Answer) Yes, I have no choice. (Question) Does your husband have any property in his hometown? (Answer) No. (Question) Does the defendant have parents or siblings? (Answer) He is the only child. Judge Zhao then invited Prosecutor Wang to the court to express his opinion, and the lawyers of both parties debated each other once, considering it concluded and awaiting judgment.

A Car Runs Over a Girl's Leg 123

Yu Dawanzi, a native of Gaoyou residing at No. 4 Xiaopilong, Dongjiadu Street, Nanshi, is 29 years old. He has a daughter named Xiaomei, who is currently seven years old. At about 2 p.m. yesterday afternoon, Xiaomei went out from home and was walking along the outer road of Wangjia Wharf when a Dahua Automobile Company truck with license number 3706 came speeding along. Xiaomei was unable to avoid it and was knocked to the ground by the truck, and her right leg was crushed by the wheels. She fainted instantly and lost consciousness. Jing Ming, the police officer on duty at the 15th checkpoint, heard the news and rushed to the scene. He first took the injured person to Shanghai Hospital for treatment and arrested the driver of the truck, Liu Shousong, a native of Yangzhou, and took him to the First Precinct, First Sub-station. After a preliminary interrogation by the station chief, the case was related to injury, and he ordered that a document be prepared and sent to the Shanghai Local Court for investigation.

Municipal Government Organization Rules 126

The Shanghai Municipal Government, following instructions from the National Government, drafted organizational rules and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for approval. The following is an excerpt: (1) These rules are formulated in accordance with Article 21 of the Municipal Organization Law. (2) This Municipal Government, in accordance with Articles 1 and 2 of the Municipal Organization Law, is named the Shanghai Municipal Government and is directly under the jurisdiction of the Executive Yuan. (3) The municipal area shall be the administrative scope of the city as approved by the National Government. (4) This Municipal Government, in accordance with the provisions of Article 11 of the Municipal Organization Law, shall administer municipal administrative affairs and supervise subordinate agencies and autonomous organizations. (5) This Municipal Government shall have one Mayor who shall direct and supervise subordinate personnel. (6) This Municipal Government shall have two Councilors, appointed or recommended, who shall be responsible for drafting and reviewing municipal single regulations or orders. (7) This Municipal Government shall have the following departments and bureaus: (1) Secretariat, (2) Social Affairs Bureau, (3) Public Safety Bureau, (4) Finance Bureau, (5) Public Works Bureau, (6) Education Bureau, (7) Health Bureau, (8) Land Bureau, (9) Public Utilities Bureau. (8) The Secretariat shall have one Secretary-General, appointed or recommended, three Secretaries, recommended, three Section Chiefs, recommended, and thirty-six to forty-eight Section Staff, appointed. (9) The Secretariat shall be responsible for documentation, general affairs, and other matters not belonging to the various bureaus. (10) The Social Affairs Bureau shall have one Director, appointed or recommended, four Section Chiefs, recommended, twenty-five to thirty-five Section Staff, appointed, two to three Technicians, recommended, and sixteen to eighteen Technical Assistants, recommended. (11) The Social Affairs Bureau shall have the following duties: (1) Household registration and personnel registration matters, (2) Establishment of facilities for childcare, elderly care, poverty relief, and disaster relief, etc., (3) Grain storage and regulation matters, (4) Improvement and protection of agriculture, industry, and commerce, (5) Labor administration matters, (6) Protection and prohibition of afforestation, land reclamation, animal husbandry, and hunting, (7) Organization and guidance of cooperatives and mutual assistance enterprises, (8) Customs improvement matters. (12) The Public Safety Bureau shall have one Director, appointed or recommended, three Section Chiefs, recommended, one Chief Inspector, recommended, fifty to sixty Section Staff, recommended, and twenty-eight to thirty-six Inspectors, appointed. (13) The Public Safety Bureau shall divide its jurisdiction into several districts, each with one District Chief, appointed. Each district shall be divided into several stations, each with one Station Chief, appointed. The water area shall have a Water Patrol Team with one Team Leader, appointed. In addition, for the purpose of apprehending thieves and suppressing criminals, or dealing with emergencies, a Detective Team and a Police Battalion shall be established, each with one Team Leader, appointed. (14) The Public Safety Bureau may establish a Police Training School to train police officers. (15) The Public Safety Bureau shall have the following duties: (1) Public safety matters, (2) Fire prevention matters. (16) The Finance Bureau shall have one Director, appointed or recommended, three Section Chiefs, recommended, and thirty-five to forty-five Section Staff, appointed. (17) The Finance Bureau shall have the following duties: (1) Financial revenue and budget and final account preparation matters, (2) Management and disposal of public property. (18) The Public Works Bureau shall have one Director, appointed or recommended, five Section Chiefs, recommended, ten to fifteen Section Staff, appointed, eight to twelve Technicians, recommended, and twenty-five to thirty-five Technical Assistants, appointed. (19) The Public Works Bureau shall have the following duties: (1) Construction and repair of public buildings, parks, public sports grounds, public cemeteries, etc., (2) Guidance and prohibition of citizen construction, (3) Roads, bridges, ditches, embankments, and other public civil engineering projects, (4) River and port affairs. (20) The Education Bureau shall have one Director, appointed or recommended, four Section Chiefs, recommended, twenty-five to thirty-five Section Staff, appointed, four Supervisors, recommended or appointed, and twelve to sixteen Inspectors, appointed. (21) The Education Bureau shall have the following duties: (1) Education matters, (2) Other cultural matters. (22) The Health Bureau shall have one Director, appointed or recommended, three Section Chiefs, recommended, six to nine Section Staff, appointed, three to four Technicians, recommended, and twenty to thirty Technical Assistants, appointed. (23) The Health Bureau shall have the following duties: (1) Public health matters, (2) Establishment and prohibition of hospitals, vegetable markets, slaughterhouses, and public entertainment venues, etc. (24) The Land Bureau shall have one Director, appointed or recommended, four Section Chiefs, recommended, sixteen to twenty-four Section Staff, appointed, four to six Technicians, recommended, and sixteen to twenty-four Technical Assistants, appointed. (25) The Land Bureau shall have the following duties: (1) Land administration matters. (26) The Public Utilities Bureau shall have one Director, appointed or recommended, four Section Chiefs, recommended, twenty to thirty Section Staff, appointed, six to ten Technicians, recommended, and fifteen to twenty-five Technical Assistants, appointed. (27) The Public Utilities Bureau shall have the following duties: (1) Water, electricity, and transportation matters, (2) Supervision of public utilities operated by private and other government agencies, (3) Operation and management of public enterprises. (28) If it is necessary for the various bureaus under the Municipal Government to establish a secretariat, it shall be submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. (29) The Municipal Government and its various departments and bureaus may hire specialized personnel as needed, with the approval of the Executive Yuan. (30) The Municipal Government and its various departments and bureaus may employ clerks and employees as appropriate. (31) The Municipal Government and its various departments and bureaus may establish affiliated agencies as needed, with the approval of the Executive Yuan. (32) The working rules for the various departments and bureaus under the Municipal Government shall be formulated separately. (33) The Municipal Government Conference shall be conducted in accordance with the provisions of Articles 24 to 27 of the Municipal Organization Law. (34) The detailed rules for the Municipal Government Conference shall be formulated separately. (35) If there are any matters not covered by these rules, the Mayor may submit them to the Municipal Government Conference for resolution and submit them to the Executive Yuan for amendment. (36) These rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation upon approval by the Executive Yuan.

Tax Rules Association 127

Telegraph Request to Exempt Business Tax from Zhuang Customers

And Should Levy Tax on Industries

The Tax Rules Research Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Trade Associations, regarding the Fujian Provincial Department of Finance's levy of business tax on timber Zhuang customers, specially telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to stop it. The text reads: "Respectfully to the Ministry of Finance of the Nanjing National Government, after investigation, Zhuang customers who only buy and do not sell, and who have no business income, should be exempt from business tax. This was approved by the Ministry's Order No. 5754 and distributed to the Finance Departments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces to comply with. Recently, we received a letter from the Shanghai Timber Trade Association stating that our members send people to Fujian to set up Zhuang in Zhongzhou to purchase timber, which is entirely buying and not selling, and there is no business income, so there is no need to pay business tax in that province. However, we recently received letters and telegrams from Zhuang customers stationed in Fujian, all stating that the Provincial Department of Finance has now changed the abolished consumption tax on bamboo and wood to a business tax on bamboo and wood, and on May 1st, it set up a bureau and sent personnel along the Zhongzhou River to collect taxes by force. After recording and reporting to the Ministry and requesting exemption, the Ministry claimed that they had not seen any explicit documents and could not verify it. The provincial business tax in Fujian, which levies taxes on goods, is inconsistent with the revised Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial business tax regulations of the Ministry, which stipulate that taxes should be levied on industries. It is even more against the Ministry's orders to force Zhuang customers who only buy and do not sell to pay business tax. We hereby report the situation and request that you review and instruct them to correct it to comply with the law and be convenient for the public. Respectfully, Shanghai Municipal Trade Associations Tax Rules Research Committee."

Obscene Harassment of Female Workers is Detestable 128

Cheng Genbao, a 16-year-old girl from Wuxi, is currently working in a sock factory near the Shanghai Army Camp in the Nanshi area. She lives at No. 335 Dongjiadu Street. Yesterday morning around 7 o'clock, Genbao went to the factory to work as usual. Unexpectedly, when she was passing through the Lujiabang area, three men suddenly came up, seeing that Genbao was alone and could be bullied, and followed her. At that time, it happened to be raining, and they did not have umbrellas, so they saw Genbao holding a parasol. They rushed up in a crowd and said, "Sister, where are you going? It's raining heavily, and our clothes are all wet. Thank you, can we share your umbrella to avoid the rain?" Genbao did not say a word. They took the opportunity to tease her. Genbao was extremely angry and rebuked them. The three men became angry out of shame and started cursing each other. Then they beat Genbao. The girl was weak and dared not resist. Fortunately, she grabbed one of the three men on the spot and shouted for the guard police at the 22nd post of the area, who took him to the First Section of the First District. The other two had already escaped. When the director of the station interrogated him, the man confessed his name was Zhang Xinghua, 19 years old, a local, and currently an apprentice at the Daxing Machine Factory on Zhonghua Road. Pudong People Selling Counterfeit Money 132

Principal Offender and Related Persons Detained

Recently, Lu Ada from Pudong has been specializing in selling counterfeit money in the city, selling it for 30 yuan per hundred yuan. Most of those who are unafraid of the law and only seek profit buy it and use it to deceive others, disrupting the financial system, which is truly hateful. The police station has repeatedly received reports, but because the transaction location is extremely secret, investigation is not easy, and it is difficult to solve the case. The other day, detective Feng Zhiming finally learned that they were buying and selling at the Lao Xinfang Hotel at No. 36 Jingyuan Street, so he sent his assistant Zhu Shengquan to pretend to be a buyer and visited Lu in room 11. After agreeing on the amount and value of the purchase, they agreed on a time for delivery. Zhu then reported back to detective Feng and led detectives to surround and arrest them. Besides Lu Ada, Jin Yuxiang, Ma Yongrui (aka Ma Arong), Zhang Xigen, and others from his hometown were also in the room and were arrested. Lu was found to have ten ten-yuan counterfeit bills and fifty five-yuan counterfeit bills in his possession, all of which were searched out. They were then sent to the Special District Local Court for investigation. Lu, Jin, and Ma confessed to colluding to sell counterfeit money. However, Zhang Xigen confessed that Jin was his brother-in-law and that he went to the hotel to ask Jin for a loan of 40 yuan and was arrested along with him. Judge Xu instructed all the defendants to be detained for another hearing. Zhang Xigen was allowed to be released on bail if he could provide a security deposit of 1,000 yuan or a substantial store. The location of the counterfeiting machine is still under investigation.

(6) Regarding the Chen Xiangxing Printing House's unreasonable deduction of wages by the employer, it was resolved to send Liang Yuling to be responsible for handling it. (7) The Xin Yi Branch reported that the employer dismissed workers without reason. It was resolved to convene a small group meeting of the branch first. The meeting adjourned at 12:00.

Fifth District Cotton Spinning Industry Labor Union: A temporary board meeting was held on the 8th. Chairman Zhang Qingyun discussed the following items: (1) The factory refused to allow workers to work. How to handle this? It was resolved to elect Wang Ayuan and others as representatives to petition the Social Affairs Bureau, requesting that the factory be ordered to open immediately and that wages be paid as usual during the shutdown period. (2) Can the factory's filling in the insurance policy be recognized? It was resolved that it will not be recognized without the approval of the Social Affairs Bureau. (3) How to handle workers who were detained for no reason? It was resolved to request the Social Affairs Bureau to order the factory to release them immediately.

Sixth District Knitting Industry Labor Union: The Fourth Joint Meeting of the Board of Directors and Supervisors was held on the 8th. Chairman Xu Chunfa discussed the following items: (1) The union has received instructions from the Social Affairs Bureau to change the Zhabei District Knitting Industry Labor Union to the Sixth District Knitting Industry Labor Union. It was resolved to approve it. (2) The union's former address at No. 124 Zhonghua Xin Road has expired. It was resolved to select No. 49 Anlefang, Zhonghua Xin Road, as the new address and to report it to the higher authorities for record by the Documentary Affairs Section. It was resolved to approve it. (3) Xu Chunfa proposed that the union's affairs could not proceed due to the lack of staff and proposed hiring Hu Peiji as the general secretary. Please make a public decision. It was resolved that the union would hire him additionally. (4) Zhou Jixin proposed that the economic aspect was very important and proposed adding a chief accountant to be in charge of all accounts. It was resolved to hire Cheng Xiangsheng as the chief accountant and to send a written invitation by the General Affairs Section. (5) It was proposed that the accounts and all equipment of the former Yihe Factory Workers' Union should be urged to be handed over by the previous committee members. It was resolved that the previous committee members should formally hand over the accounts within one week. (6) It was proposed that the nameplate of the former Zhabei District Knitting Industry Labor Union should be changed due to the change of name. How to handle this? It was resolved that Xu Chunfa and Chen Asan should be responsible for handling it. (7) Gu Lunbu, Yang Dehua, and He Shiyuan, three directors of the Hua Chun Factory, often missed meetings. Please make a public decision. It was resolved that the Documentary Affairs Section should send written notices to Gu Lunbu, etc., and limit the shortest period for reply.

Cai Zhengya's Speech on Recent Labor Issues in Shanghai 139

The Chinese Industrial and Commercial Management Association previously held a meeting at the Lianhua General Association, inviting statistics expert Cai Zhengya to give a speech entitled "Recent Labor Issues in Shanghai." We have obtained the original manuscript and are publishing it below:

The Industrial and Commercial Management Association is a group dedicated to studying issues related to industrial and commercial management. But how should we approach the study of these issues? First, we need to briefly discuss the attitude we should adopt. When approaching a problem to be studied, we should first adopt an objective, impartial, and unbiased attitude to collect materials. The goal is to understand the actual content of the issue, not to predict what it should be. Only with facts can we have a basis for research and seek methods for improvement. Therefore, I hope to briefly discuss the recent labor situation in Shanghai today. Everyone here is a prominent figure in the business world, and time is precious. If I can provide you with some important information regarding labor issues as a basis for discussion, then I won't have wasted your valuable time. However, to make a concise observation of the extremely complex labor issues in Shanghai in a very short period of time will inevitably lead to omissions. Now, I will select a few important matters to discuss.

(1) Labor-Capital Disputes: Labor-capital disputes are a very important issue between labor and capital recently. Strikes are the method used by labor to deal with capital, temporarily ceasing work to achieve their demands. Lockouts are the method used by capital to deal with labor, temporarily suspending work to achieve the demands of capital. Now, let's put aside cases of labor-capital disputes that did not lead to strikes or lockouts. Let's first look at the figures for strikes and lockouts in the entire city in the last three years, 1928, 1929, and 1930, to observe the situation. In 1928, there were 120 strike cases, involving 5,438 factories, 213,966 workers, 3,010,926 lost workdays, and a loss of $1,592,593 in wages. In 1929, there were 111 strike and lockout cases, involving 1,512 factories, 68,867 workers, 751,146 lost workdays, and a loss of $488,695 in wages. In 1930, there were 87 strike and lockout cases, involving 672 factories, 63,802 workers, 810,102 lost workdays, and a loss of $469,477 in wages. Lockout cases were very few, only a few each year. Observing the figures for the past three years, it can be seen that the labor unrest in 1928 was very serious. Afterwards, the situation eased and gradually trended downwards. Now, let's talk about the main causes of disputes. Over the years, there have been many reasons for labor-capital disputes, but they are always concentrated on four aspects: wages, hiring and firing, collective agreements, and treatment. In 1928, cases arising from wage issues accounted for 22.5% of the total cases for the year, those arising from hiring or firing accounted for 20.0%, those arising from collective agreements accounted for 14.1%, and those arising from treatment issues accounted for 67.5%. In 1929, cases arising from wage issues accounted for 23.4% of the total cases for the year, those arising from hiring or firing accounted for 32.4%, those arising from collective agreements accounted for 14.4%, and those arising from treatment issues accounted for 9.9%. In 1930, cases arising from wage issues accounted for 41.4% of the total cases for the year, those arising from hiring or firing accounted for 14.9%, those arising from collective agreements accounted for 13.8%, and those arising from treatment issues accounted for 10.3%. The above figures tell us that in 1928, cases arising from the four items of wages, hiring or firing, collective agreements, and treatment accounted for 67.5% of the total cases for the year, 80.2% in 1929, and 80.5% in 1930. Among these four items, wages are the most important, followed by hiring or firing. If we want to promote labor-capital cooperation, we should first study these four fundamental issues. Now, let's look at the figures for the results of disputes, which can represent the attitudes of both labor and capital and the trends in their negotiating power. In 1928, cases where the labor side's demands were fully accepted by the capital side accounted for 38.5% of the total cases for the year, those where the capital side partially accepted accounted for 33.3%, and those where the capital side did not accept accounted for 10.5%. There were no cases where the capital side made demands. In 1929, cases where the labor side's demands were fully accepted by the capital side accounted for 28.8% of the total cases for the year, those where the capital side partially accepted accounted for 36.9%, and those where the capital side did not accept accounted for 28.8%. There were no cases where the capital side demanded full acceptance by the labor side, those where the labor side partially accepted accounted for 0.9%, and those where the labor side did not accept accounted for 1.8%. In 1930, cases where the labor side's demands were fully accepted by the capital side accounted for 24.1%, those where the capital side partially accepted accounted for 43.7%, and those where the capital side did not accept accounted for 25.3%. There were no cases where the capital side demanded full acceptance by the labor side, those where the labor side partially accepted accounted for 4.6%, and those where the labor side did not accept accounted for 1.3%. The above figures tell us that the cases where the labor side's demands were fully accepted have significantly decreased, and the cases where the labor side's demands were not accepted have increased. Although the cases where the labor side's demands were partially accepted have also increased, in 1929 and 1930, the capital side even began to make demands for the labor side to accept, which was unprecedented. From this, it can be seen that the labor side can no longer demand anything from the capital side as it did in the past. In other words, the capital side is gradually able to defend against the attacks of the labor side and has begun to attack the labor side.

(2) Wages and Working Hours: When it comes to the wages and working hours of Shanghai workers, our materials are limited to factory workers, not including handicraft workers. There are a total of 21 important industries in this city. These 21 industries have a total of 2,326 factories. If we follow the regulations of the Factory Law, which stipulates that only those with 30 or more employees can be called factories, then there are only 697 factories. Regardless of this regulation, these 21 industries have a total of 285,700 workers. Regarding wages and working hours, workers' income can be divided into two types: one is the fixed wage rate, paid by the hour or by the piece, and issued periodically; the other is the actual income, which is the fixed wage plus bonuses, dividends, or rice subsidies, etc., minus the deductions. According to the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau's report on wages and working hours for 1929, I have calculated the figures for male, female, and child labor separately, based on the number of people in each industry, as follows: the average daily wage rate for male workers is $0.75, the average monthly actual income is $24.43, and the average daily working hours are 10.5 hours; the average daily wage rate for female workers is $0.50, the average monthly actual income is $12.73, and the average daily working hours are 11.5 hours; the average daily wage rate for child workers is $0.36, the average monthly actual income is $8.70, and the average daily working hours are 10.7 hours. The overall average for male, female, and child labor is a daily wage rate of $0.57, a monthly actual income of $15.95, and daily working hours of 10.8 hours. The above figures are for workers with varying wages in all 21 industries. Among these 21 industries, if we determine the importance of an industry based on the number of people it employs, then cotton spinning and silk reeling are the most important. These two industries account for 41% of the total number of people employed in the 21 industries. The wages of workers in these two industries are relatively low, and the working hours are also relatively long. This is because workers in these two industries do not necessarily need to undergo a long period of training to be competent. Therefore, their skills cannot be said to be very strong or important, so their wages are also relatively low. The average daily wage rate for female workers in the cotton spinning industry is only $0.452, the average monthly actual income is only $12.50, and the working hours are nearly 12 hours. The average daily wage rate for female workers in the silk reeling industry is $0.539, the average monthly actual income is $13.22, and the working hours are nearly 11 hours. These two industries rely heavily on female labor, so I am only discussing the wages of female workers. This can also be said to be a model figure for Shanghai factory workers.

(3) Cost of Living: To study labor issues, we must not only ask about the income of workers, but we must also ask about their expenses. What is the average annual cost of living for a worker's family? What percentage of the total cost of living is accounted for by the five categories of clothing, food, housing, fuel, and miscellaneous items? Is the trend of living expenses for Shanghai workers upward or downward? Although the cost of living index compiled by the Tariff Commission of the Ministry of Finance is limited to yarn factory workers in this city, it is sufficient to represent a glimpse of the living conditions of ordinary workers. The percentages of these five types of expenses are distributed as follows: food accounts for 56.0%, clothing accounts for 9.4%, rent accounts for 6.4%, fuel accounts for 7.5%, and miscellaneous items account for 20.6%. The above figures tell us that the largest expense for workers is food, followed by miscellaneous items. Miscellaneous items include all other expenses, such as hygiene, education, entertainment, etc., which are of course included. If we analyze it carefully, we will know that the expenses for hygiene, entertainment, and education are indeed pitifully small. The average annual expense for entertainment for a family is only $1.07, and education is $0.77. The monotonous life of workers, the inability to improve the level of workers' education, and the inability to develop advanced skills are natural consequences. The changes and trends in the cost of living for workers in this city can be seen in the cost of living index. This index uses 1926 as the standard for comparison. The expenses in this year are equal to 100, the index for 1928 is 102.5, for 1929 it is 107.9, and for 1930 it is 121.4. These figures indicate that the cost of living has increased significantly in recent years. In 1930, there was a very significant increase. One important reason is the impact of the high price of gold and the low price of silver, which led to rising prices. When prices rise, the purchasing power of money shrinks. This sudden increase in the cost of living is by no means matched by the rate of increase in wages, which makes the lives of workers even more miserable. In addition, there are many important issues such as unemployment, labor agreements, labor laws, labor organizations, and labor movements, which I will not discuss today due to time constraints. Now, let me summarize what I have said above. Since the National Revolutionary Army occupied Shanghai in 1927, until the first half of 1928, due to political changes and the instigation of the Communist Party, the labor community in Shanghai can be said to have been in a state of extreme excitement. Strikes occurred everywhere. Under this force, employers had no choice but to endure. This period can be said to be a period when the labor community rose and employers succumbed. From the second half of 1928, peace and order gradually returned, and labor laws were gradually created. The period of storms and waves in the past slowly passed. By 1929, labor administration had gradually become regulated. Labor-capital disputes gradually decreased. This period can be said to be a period when the labor movement was managed and supervised by the government. In 1930, employers were oppressed by the high price of gold and the low price of silver and the sluggishness of the industry, and they had to strive for survival. Although labor victories in labor-capital disputes still accounted for the majority, the attitude of employers hardened, and they did not easily give in. Sometimes, they even took an aggressive stance towards labor. This is a period of self-awareness and self-determination for employers. These three periods are very obvious. After several years of turmoil and disputes, it is now gradually getting on the right track. We very much hope to reach the fourth period, which is the period of labor-capital cooperation. Workers' wages, working hours, and cost of living are issues that are closely related to the labor side and should be resolved based on facts. The production of high-quality products and the increase in production are the keys to the development of industry and commerce. The more effort the Chinese people put in, the more the total amount of the national economy will increase. Dr. Sun Yat-sen said that the interests of both labor and capital are complementary, and the evolution of society depends entirely on the cooperation of the people. It can be seen that Dr. Sun Yat-sen paid close attention to labor-capital cooperation.
