World Snippets 140

— Hai Ke

According to experiments conducted by a large factory in northern England, flies will fly away when they see a house with yellow glass windows, and they dare not approach it. They also do not like rooms with blue painted walls. Therefore, if you want to avoid fly infestations in the summer, you may want to use yellow glass windows and blue painted walls.

The consumption of coffee by Americans averages 13 pounds per person per year. In the United Kingdom, proportionally, the average is only about half a pound per person per year.

Due to the large population and busy streets in London, traffic accidents are common. According to statistics from 1927, there were as many as 850 incidents. A large store lost 41,135 hours of office time due to this.

The Bay of Biscay, located north of France and Spain, has extremely clear water. The water used to raise aquatic animals in the London Zoo Aquarium is taken from here.

Among infectious diseases, there is a disease called foot-and-mouth disease, which is transmitted from animals. Between 1928 and 1929, the United Kingdom slaughtered 14,000 animals due to the spread of this disease.

United Celebration of All Circles in the Capital Amidst the Sound of the National Assembly 141

— Ding Ming

Motorcade Parade in the Joyful Rain on May 4th. A sweet rain fell. Although I did not go out, I was informed by a friend in a letter that at 1:30 pm that afternoon, more than 30 cars from various agencies gathered at the Public Sports Field on Park Road. At 2:00 pm, they set off in the rain. The military band led the way, with the command headquarters on both sides, issuing orders. There was a discipline department maintaining order. The procession passed through Huapailou, Zhongshan Road, Taiping Bridge, Yijiangmen, Drum Tower, Shiqiao Street, Shuiximen Street, Ziwu Road, Nanmen Street, Confucius Temple, Qiwang Street, Zhongzheng Street, and other places, distributing leaflets along the way. The spectators were like walls. The procession returned to the starting point and disbanded.

Lantern Parade Wrapped in Gentle Breeze after Dinner. I heard the sound of a flute, clear, melodious and pleasant. I rushed to see it, and saw everyone holding a paper red lantern, with the seven characters "Celebrating the National Assembly" pasted on the lantern. They walked in single file, one after another, on the muddy road. I heard that the forward was the Boy Scouts and male school students from all walks of life, who had already passed. Female school students followed behind, and the army brought up the rear. That evening, the rain stopped and the gentle breeze brushed, as if the heavens were helping their pleasure. It seemed to symbolize the light of our nation.

Celebration Rally Everyone Was Excited At 2:00 pm on the afternoon of May 5th, a rally to celebrate the National Assembly was held at the Public Sports Field. I did not go either. I heard that after the meeting opened as scheduled, representatives from the National Assembly, the Central Party Headquarters, the National and Municipal Governments, and various sectors gave speeches one after another. At the end, they shouted slogans and played music to end the meeting. Party and state dignitaries and the masses were all very excited.

Everyone Welcomed in Front of the Entertainment Stage After 8:00 pm, I sat in a rickshaw, bumping through the streets paved with rough stones. All along the way, there were teams of soldiers, some on horseback and some on foot. The sounds of rickshaws and cars advancing and retreating, and the stingy old man hobbling and slipping, were all interesting sights. Passing over Fucheng Bridge, the Qinhuai River runs horizontally north and south like a wriggling cyan dragon. The surrounding night was hazy, decorated with only a few electric torches. Turning south and passing through the First Park to Park Road, the three characters "Supervisory Yuan" formed by countless electric light bulbs were prominently displayed in the center of the archway standing tall in the blue sky. After another few steps, I entered the south gate of the venue. Looking around, there were mountains and seas of people. The entertainment stage was divided into three venues. I first went to the new drama performance area in the southwest corner. There, eight people, including martyrs, women, young men, and blind people, stood on either side, singing pure songs together. Due to the extreme crowding, I was unable to move forward and listen carefully, so I couldn't tell what song it was. However, there were three blind women wearing sunglasses, raising their heads and chests, and frequently moving their heads left and right. If it weren't for one blind woman and four blind men without glasses truthfully revealing their identities on their left, people would have thought they were sighted. I then went to the southeast, where a movie was being shown, "The Family of New People." I returned to the northwest to watch Peking Opera, where three scenes of "Beating the Drum and Scolding Cao" were being performed simultaneously. It was overwhelming, so some people stood in one corner, staring intently without moving, while others moved around, sometimes southeast, sometimes northwest, and sometimes southeast again, unable to decide where to go. I walked around the venue once and estimated that I saw no fewer than ten thousand people. I returned and analyzed it carefully, and found that there were the most people watching Peking Opera, as they were mostly the uneducated masses. Those watching the new drama were the next most numerous, and they were mostly people from the lower and middle classes of society. Those watching the movie were the least numerous, and they were mostly people from the upper and middle classes. This certainly varies according to each individual's preferences, but it is also sufficient to show a glimpse of the psychology of the masses and the level of the nation. As for gender, men accounted for almost the entire number, while women were as rare as morning stars. However, whether they were fathers and sons, brothers, husbands and wives, or friends, they were all in pairs, rejoicing and cheering. Only I was a solitary person, coming and going alone, and I couldn't help but feel sad and returned home despondently.

Madam Zhong's Birthday 142

— Cheng Zhizheng

On the 30th of last month, Mr. Zhong Weicheng, Dean of the School of Management at Jiaotong University, celebrated his mother's sixtieth birthday at the Dongfang Hotel. For a time, the leaders and scholars of Shanghai gathered together, bustling about, creating an unprecedented grand occasion. Mr. Zhong is a well-known figure in the transportation industry, so the birthday banners and couplets hanging on the four walls were mostly from the transportation industry. Sun Zhesheng, Wang Boqun, Ye Yuhu, Li Zhaohuan, Huang Hanliang, Gao Jiyi, and other gentlemen all personally wrote birthday couplets to offer their congratulations. Among them, the couplet by Mr. Huang Hanliang was particularly exquisite, reaching a wonderful realm. The couplet read, "The hardships of the past have made a far-reaching ambition, and today, a cup of wine comforts the heart of the loved one." It was most able to transcend the mundane. At 6:00 pm, everyone took their seats, and President Li of Jiaotong University also attended. Everyone vied to tease him to drink. Dr. Li Quanshi, an economist, happened to be present and was also affected. The sound of laughter filled the entire evening, reaching the outside. In the evening, the Peking Opera Troupe of Jiaotong University performed a gala, including "Chen Xizhi's Female Escort" and "Xu Houzhi's Iron Bow Marriage," all of which were extremely wonderful. The play ended late at night, and everyone returned home tipsy.

The Future of Human Teeth 143

— Lü Bing

There is a European saying, "I hope we don't use our teeth too much." Its meaning is probably that chewing too much can harm the body, while dieting can often ward off illness. But studying human teeth, it is certain that the shape of the teeth and bones of modern men and women is indeed narrower than that of ancient people, and there is a tendency for them to become more and more delicate. Examining the reasons, it is not related to the amount of language used that causes changes, but rather the difference in food between ancient and modern people that has led to this.

A certain scientist who specializes in the study of dental problems once gave a speech, saying that the food we eat today is becoming increasingly soft, making it easier to digest and eliminating the need for chewing by the gums. Therefore, as the movement of the teeth is reduced, they will inevitably gradually degenerate and become narrow and delicate. However, this change actually makes the teeth appear more beautiful when women smile shallowly.

Sir Kader collected thousands of ancient and modern human skulls and jaws throughout his life. According to his report, the teeth of people from earlier times were generally large and sparse, strong and powerful, so fine teeth were rarely seen. This is because in ancient times, the food was not refined and was mostly coarse and tough. It was impossible to solve the problem of survival without the strength of the teeth. The teeth of the future are naturally continuing to change, but the extent to which they will change cannot be predicted at present. However, a certain scholar recently told someone that he imagined that a century from now, the teeth of human beings in the world will be as slender as a rabbit's. Although the words are humorous, they are also sufficient to show that human teeth are indeed becoming more and more delicate.

Mourning Ji Mei 144

— Huo Meng

My old friend, Mr. Wang Meiqu (who later changed his name to Mei Ju), was a descendant of famous officials who accumulated virtue and had talent for writing. His works were numerous, and he enjoyed a reputation in the literary world. He maintained his career for decades without changing it. Even in poverty, he was content. He was over sixty years old, and his spirit was not diminished. I was hoping that he would live to be eighty or ninety years old. However, ten days ago, in the cold spring, the medicine stove had just been lit when he suddenly passed away on May 4, 1931, at his residence at 1178 Qian Shan Lane, Avenue Edward VII. He was sixty-six years old. Two days later, at the beginning of summer, his funeral was held at the Shanghai Lianyi Villa, where he was buried. Mr. Wang was a native of Haikang, Guangdong. On that day, the sky was covered with dark clouds, and heavy rain continued to fall. Many people held the ropes, and their clothes were soaked. Could it be that the so-called dust was cleared from the road to welcome Mr. Wang to the realm of immortals? I remember that I met Mr. Wang at the West Lake. Every time the plum blossoms were in full bloom, we would hold wine in Gushan. The wine stains on my clothes can still be clearly recognized today. Recently, Mr. Wang was employed by Mr. Du in Panyu. We met again in Shanghai and became even closer. For more than ten years, we shared our ideals and formed a friendship between teacher and friend. I deeply admired his humility and grace, which made him all the more admirable and approachable. He was a rare find. He must have obtained his carefree spirit from the mountains and forests. The wind turned the white banners, and I recalled his words and deeds. How could I not feel the loss of a person and a lyre? Mr. Wang never stopped reading for decades. He once said that it was the greatest joy to educate the talented people of the world. Therefore, he planted peach and plum trees in his vast courtyard. I once jokingly called him Mr. Jianzhai, but Mr. Wang modestly said, "I am not capable." I said, "Then you are higher than Jian." We laughed together. When I look back on it now, his words are still in my ears, but Mr. Wang has passed away. Mr. Wang was fond of drinking and eating, and he even made a food list. From now on, the spring mornings when we cut chives and the autumn nights when we held crabs will be most difficult. Where are my old friends? Thinking of this, I cannot help but feel sad. Life is like a dream, and the yellow beam is already ripe. I cannot help but feel sad for Mr. Wang, but also happy for him. The clothes, coffin, and burial ground were all willingly provided by Mr. Du. Everything was beautiful and complete in the southeast. The deceased rests peacefully in his resting place. If Mr. Wang is conscious in the underworld, he should be comforted. There are people in the world who are indifferent to their dead friends. How can they not be ashamed when they hear of this? Mr. Wang has two sons who will inherit his virtue and can be sure that they will not change their ways in three years. (Qiao Chou)

Correction: In the article "Hu Pu'an's Poem "Great Aspirations" published on May 4, the character "茳" in the fourth line of Mr. Hu's original poem "渺渺春波釆綠茳" was mistakenly printed as "茫". In the sixth line, the character "母" in "慣經泛宅母勞卜" was mistakenly printed as "母". We hereby correct this error.

Travel Notes from India (49) 145

— Linghua

Arrived in Allahabad at eleven o'clock. Staying at Professor Ranjan's house. I have been traveling through various parts of India for several months. Everywhere I look, there are countless PhDs. Hundreds of professors. It's not unusual to see hundreds of PhDs at a large gathering. They are all intellectuals. This class is generally also capitalist. They have cars and gardens. I think if they were to encounter Mr. Marx, they would definitely be in danger, because they are all capitalist and intellectual. However, I have a deep feeling. Even if the intellectual class does not encounter Mr. Marx, they are truly useless. Looking at the universities of India, they are like forests. PhDs are like leaves. But they cannot save the country from ruin, nor can they save the poor from starvation. Alas, education is bankrupt. PhDs are bankrupt. The intellectual class also declares itself bankrupt. India is truly worthy of being called a civilized country. No wonder they despise world culture, but Indians cannot solve politics. That is their shortcoming. Because historically they are not a political nation, but a religious nation. Indians have no political history. They do not pay attention to the rise and fall of dynasties. They only pay attention to religious philosophy. To this day, they are still a model teacher for all nations. How great. Alas. What about politics?

The twelfth. Met Indian leader Gandhi. Mahatma Gandhi. He lives in the house of Motilal Nehru in Mati. Motilal Nehru has great power. Millions in wealth. And is an old friend of Gandhi. When I gave a lecture at the Allahabad Student Association, the students distributed flyers. Asking me to speak. The flyer boldly wished Motilal Nehru a long life. I didn't know why. Now I know that he is an important person working with Gandhi. Gandhi is the teacher. That he is the leader. But unfortunately, after the students wished him a long life, he died in Lucknow. He was seventy years old. All of India mourned. But his son can succeed his father. I first met his son. The son's name is Jawaharlal Nehru. Not yet thirty years old, very elegant. I heard that his wife is also strong. Jawaharlal Nehru has traveled to Russia. Rich in knowledge. Gandhi is still his teacher. Almost like assisting a young lord. Invisibly, it is the People's Government of India. Because there are great people behind Gandhi. I visited Gandhi. At nine o'clock in the morning. Many cars in front of the door. Professor Ranjan, in whose house I was staying, said. He has never been able to see Gandhi in his life. Because Gandhi has become the uncrowned king of all of India. In my life, I am most afraid of talking about equality. I said that the word equality was used by Rousseau in the eighteenth century as a tool to call on citizens to revolt against the government. To start a great revolution. When Mr. Sun Yat-sen was in Guangzhou, he had great difficulties because some people misunderstood it. In order to unite the masses. He created eight ranks to explain it. Now I meet Gandhi. Gandhi is of course an extremely equal uncrowned emperor. However, he lives in a large foreign building. Cars in front of the door are like clouds. University professors cannot even see him. Meeting time is extremely valuable. No different from headquarters. Alas. People who are superstitious about equality. That is why there are so many injustices in the world.

Rotary Club novel

Hawthorne's Detective Case - A Twist (10) 146

— Cheng Xiaoqing

(4) The Necklace Problem

At this moment, Zhang Baoquan also realized the seriousness of the case and shifted his gaze. He re-examined the necklace on the table, then wrapped it up again with the white cloth. He asked me, "Mr. Bao, what do you think is the nature of this case? Could it be a robbery case?" I replied, "There are several possibilities here, all of which could be true. However, one of these possibilities is closest to the facts before us. I saw my aunt, Ms. Peifen, wearing a pearl necklace tonight. Since this bandit also came out of the Gao family's house, this thing is clearly my aunt's." Zhang Baoquan said, "This understanding is indeed very close. But the thing is already in his hands, why would he lightly throw it away? Even if he suspects someone is following him, he can simply throw the stolen goods somewhere hidden for later retrieval. Now that he has moved the stolen goods into your hands, hasn't he worked in vain?" I said, "This is his cunning. He handed the stolen goods to me, clearly to divert the pursuer's attention, making people believe that I am his accomplice. The pursuer's goal is primarily the stolen goods. He can naturally escape safely. Otherwise, not only might the stolen goods not be saved, but he himself would also be in danger of being arrested. He sees the light and heavy very clearly. His plan is really sinister. Hasn't old Mr. Qiu already fallen for his trick?" Zhang Baoquan nodded repeatedly, expressing his admiration for my insight. He said, "Then, the first step we should take is to make a phone call to the Gao family to ask. What do you think, Mr. Bao?" I replied, "This is the obvious thing to do. I was going to call when you came back. Let me call now."

But as I stood up to go to the office to make a call, I suddenly looked up and saw a person rushing into the office in a hurry. I looked closely and it was my good friend Hawthorne. At that moment, my spirit lifted, like an army trapped in heavy encirclement suddenly receiving reinforcements. The joy in my heart was indescribable. Zhang Baoquan quickly greeted him, "Ah, Mr. Hawthorne. Long time no see. Long time no see. I never expected you to grace us with your presence tonight." Hawthorne's face showed a serious expression. He stepped forward, shook hands with Zhang Baoquan, and stopped Baoquan's greetings, immediately getting to the heart of the matter.

Speculative Silver Shows Weakness 147

Transaction Volume Is Not High

Future Looks Uncertain

Falling Six Taels and Two Mace. Speculative silver prices have been slightly sluggish this past week, but without major changes. Coinciding with the Western merchants' spring horse racing season, traditionally the market is only open for half a day, so there was not much trading volume, and prices generally fluctuated around 740 taels, with daily swings of seven or eight taels. In short, people's minds are uncertain, especially with slight changes in overseas silver markets, and incessant rumors in the market. Since speculators and major players competed to buy on Tuesday, the price once rose to 744 taels and eight mace. By Friday, sellers became aggressive and suddenly fell to 731 taels, a total difference of 13 taels and eight mace. As a result, compared to the previous weekend, it fell by six taels and two mace. The London silver bar rose by 1.875, the American silver bar was even, and the Shanghai sterling exchange rate rose by half a cent (calculated as 1.25). The Japanese gold fell by 0.0125. The actual transaction prices of banks also tended to ease. Among colleagues, there was initial selling followed by slight buying, and the exchange rate was still about 40 taels higher than the daily settlement price. As for the May futures contracts, they have now been cleared, and the spot goods are mostly held by the Central Bank, approximately 20,000 contracts in total. Therefore, the rise and fall of speculative silver prices sometimes depends on the Central Bank's trading. Currently, companies such as Fuchang, Yuanheng, Yongheng, Yuancheng, Xinheng, and Yongfeng are all short, while Daxingyong, Chenfengyong, Yutian, Yong, Bingxing, and the Guangdong-based Hengxing and Shengda are all long. Spot firms are short futures and long spot goods. However, the future of speculative silver prices is still uncertain. The general situation of this week is summarized below.

Since Monday (May 4th) was the first day of the spring races, the London silver bar rose by 1.875, the silver price remained unchanged, and the shilling rate was stable. The internal market was loose. The opening price for June speculative silver fell slightly by 0.02 taels to 744.5 taels, and continued to fall by more than 7 taels due to many sellers, settling at 37.2 taels. The Price Increased by Four to Five Taels Each Month

The yarn market situation in the first part of last week was affected by various rumors, and the American cotton market was weak. Generally, retailers were bearish and there were more sellers. Silkworm Diseases Discovered in Pinghu's Spring Silkworms 155

Heavy Rain for Two Days... Silkworms Mostly Excreted Yellow and Died

Pinghu's silkworm farmers are mostly raising improved varieties of early silkworms this year. However, due to the cold weather after the first sleep, white muscardine was discovered. When raising late silkworms, the weather was still very cold, and there was continuous spring rain, which was unfavorable for development. The early silkworms have now completed their third sleep and are sufficiently leafy. Some have even completed their large sleep. Unexpectedly, with two days of heavy rain, the silkworms all excreted yellow and were discarded, accounting for about 60%. This year's silkworm harvest is likely to be a bubble.

Book Review

Outline of Central Banking System 158

— Tang Bin

Published by Datong Bookstore

A nation's wealth and strength rely on adequate economic income and development. Moreover, the circulation of finance is of utmost importance. This is the reason for the establishment of various banking industries. Central banks are positioned in contrast to local banks and are distinguished from general banks by whether or not they have special privileges. Therefore, they are also called national banks or banks of banks. There are many interpretations of their meaning among scholars. The essential ones can be divided into four theories: (1) A central bank is the highest financial institution in a country and the center of all banks. This is the most common explanation. It means that every undertaking must have a supreme body to administer and guide it. The financial industry is particularly important. If handled improperly, its impact will ripple through the entire economic structure. The central bank leads the nation's finance, is the most complete institution in the banking system, and is located in the central hub. It constantly directs the operations of various banks, leading to national financial unity, which can be effective. This theory is relatively vague. (2) A central bank has the privilege of issuance and stands above general banks as the financial center of a country. This explanation by Japanese scholar Hidematsu Tsumura also has the drawback of being biased and incomplete. (3) The central bank reduces the responsibilities borne by general banks and restricts their powers. These are the words of American banking scholar Dunbar, which are more appropriate. (4) A central bank usually enjoys the monopoly of issuance, has a large number of branches, and is supervised by the government as an agent of the national treasury. This is the theory of J. Holdsworth, but it also fails to clarify the true meaning of a central bank. However, centralization is a necessary means adopted in modern national politics. Why should economics be any different? In today's world of ever-increasing transportation, a nation's economic prosperity or decline cannot be achieved by focusing on trivial details. Without centralizing national financial affairs, it is not possible to regulate them properly and exert the highest degree of control. Therefore, if a nation wants to concentrate financial power, it must grant various privileges to banks with great power, authorize them to engage in operations beneficial to the public, maintain and support them, and increase their authority to manipulate national finance. It should focus on the prosperity, decline, safety, and danger of the nation as a whole. When the market is in panic, it stabilizes it; when the treasury is in crisis, it rescues it, serving as the linchpin of national credit. After the collapse of the feudal system, a strong government was created in politics, and a strong bank also emerged in the financial world. This is the inevitable trend of responding to changes in the world and cannot be resisted. Here, the author offers a more definitive statement based on general interpretations:

A central bank occupies the highest position in a country's financial world, enjoys special rights, has a very close relationship with the state, does not seek private gain, and bears the great responsibility of maintaining and rescuing national credit. Therefore, it guides general banks, maintains the economy, and benefits the nation.

This interpretation of the meaning of a central bank may not fully conform to theory, but it seems to facilitate a comprehensive understanding. Regarding this, the author elaborates on it very clearly in the opening chapter of this book, making it known that a central bank has an important relationship with the state. Secondly, the functions of the central bank are briefly enumerated and divided into twelve items: (1) It can enhance the effectiveness of currency; (2) It can regulate finance; (3) It can conduct discounting; (4) It can use discount policy to stabilize finance; (5) It can cope with huge expenditures; (6) It is easy to implement banking policies; (7) It is easy to examine the national financial situation; (8) It can invigorate the operations of various localities; (9) It can develop credit transactions; (10) It can issue banknotes; (11) It can act as an agent of the national treasury; (12) It can assist national finances. In this way, we can get a glimpse of the meaning and functions of a central bank, and we can also have a concrete understanding of how it differs from general banks.

Since China has had a banking organization, it has been more than twenty years. Banking regulations have also been revised repeatedly. However, in practice, the banking industry has no system to speak of. Therefore, we can understand that the lack of a central banking system to lead the financial world has led to the proliferation of small-scale banks, numbering no less than one hundred. Although there are one or two with greater strength, their funds are still insufficient, and their operations are underdeveloped. They are unable to cope with the industry in the country, which is about to be revitalized. Since the National Government passed the Central Bank Ordinance on October 5, 1928, and officially established the Central Bank, the banking industry seems to have the hope of being rectified. However, in reality, it is not perfect. Because it coincides with the beginning of political reform and the establishment of a system, although there is no lack of commendable points, there are still many traces of compromise. Moreover, authority is chaotic, foreign power is strong, business is uneconomical, laws are not enforced, and general credit assistance institutions are not yet perfect. Furthermore, the war is not over, and the Communist bandits are destroying the rural economic organization, making it difficult to use funds. Here, the author studies the central bank of China based on the current situation and divides it into five points:

1. It is urgent to unify authority. The special rights enjoyed by the Central Bank are the issuance of banknotes and acting as an agent of the national treasury. These special rights should be granted by the government to ensure its exclusive enjoyment. Only then can the measures and facilities of the Central Bank achieve neat and uniform effects. In this way, in times of financial and fiscal distress, it can devote all its efforts to deal with it. However, if we examine the Central Bank of China, it nominally adopts a single system, but in addition to the Central Bank, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and other banks such as the Frontier Bank, the Industrial Bank, the Agricultural and Commercial Bank, the Mongolian and Tibetan Bank, and the Salt Bank also enjoy a portion of the agency privileges. As for the reorganization of banknote issuance, it is of course more important to rely on the prestige of the National Government. The banking system will be established within ten years. We should learn from the National Bank system of the United States before the European War and the United Reserve Bank system after the war, so that the speed of improvement is fast, and we should strive to do things without violating the general trend of the world and considering the domestic situation to achieve early success. 2. Business operations must be improved. Due to the depression of industry and poor credit in China, general banks either have no business to operate or are poorly managed, and they are generally on the road to failure. Therefore, general banks are competing to raise interest rates to absorb deposits, and at the same time, they are taking chances on investments to seek high profits. However, the Central Bank should not do this. That is to say, commercial banks should be commercialized, special banks should be specialized, and the Central Bank should be centralized to invigorate the nation's finance. 3. Foreign power must be eliminated urgently. Foreign banks in China, such as HSBC, Banque de l'Indochine, and Yokohama Specie Bank, are indeed hindering the national economy and the development of the Central Bank. Therefore, since the nature of the Central Bank is certain and has a strict organization, we only need to have a solid guarantee for the faithful fulfillment of foreign debts to crack down on the hegemony of foreign banks. What about the safety of keeping the funds? Now that politics is on track and the international status is increasing, we must pay attention to this, especially during the period of political tutelage and construction. 4. Laws should be implemented quickly. Since the establishment of the National Government, the Legislative Yuan has formulated various civil and commercial codes. At the time of the Central Bank's initial venture, the national economy was in a state of decline. These codes should be promulgated and implemented by the National Government as soon as possible. Then, all enterprises will obtain considerable guarantees and guidelines, the economy will naturally become super-developed, and the Central Bank can use appropriate policies to achieve unparalleled macro effects. 5. Advocate credit assistance institutions. Modern economic and social organizations are complex. If you want to develop, you must connect and help each other. The Central Bank is in a leading position and should bear the responsibility of advocating, setting up, and assisting auxiliary institutions and engaging in liaison. According to the auxiliary institutions of the bank, the most important ones are the Clearing House and the Enquiring Association. The author will also describe this in detail. Secondly, it is said that although China's central banking system is in its infancy, a careful analysis of its regulations reveals many satisfactory points, and it is also analyzed. This is indeed the most practical chapter in the study of China's central bank and is very valuable.

This book focuses on analysis and research, so the author discusses all aspects of the central bank in chapters. The evolution of central banks in various countries is only briefly described in the second chapter, including the process of establishment, the raising of capital, and the enjoyment of special rights. The organization, business, and financial manipulation policies of other central banks are discussed in chapters. It is indeed the most accurate book for studying the central banking system. It is particularly detailed about China and should be paid attention to.

New Asia Monthly 159

— Man Yin

Volume 2, Issue 1, Special Oversized Issue

"Asia is one of the five continents. In terms of area, Asia is the eldest brother. In terms of population, Asia is also the most. In terms of products, Asia also has inexhaustible resources... All the ethnic groups in Asia can stand on the roof of the world and say to all mankind, we Asians are the largest continent, our Asian history and culture are the most ancient, our Asian position and situation are the most majestic, we Asians should occupy the leading position among the five continents, we Asians should be in a leading position for the people of other continents.

But what is the actual position of the Asian continent? What is the position of the Asian people? All the ethnic groups in Asia are under severe oppression, and all the ethnic groups in Asia are in danger of extinction. The life of the Asian people is really like a thread!

China is the largest ethnic group in Asia. China's decline is the cause of the decline of all ethnic groups in Asia. China's misfortune and failure are the cause of the misfortune and failure of all ethnic groups in Asia. Therefore, the China issue is the hub of all ethnic issues in Asia. China's revitalization is the starting point for the revitalization of Asian ethnic groups..."

The above is the declaration of the inaugural issue of New Asia Monthly. Indeed, judging from the current situation, the life of the Asian people is like a thread. Asian culture has entered a path of degradation. Among them, China is the most, and China is the largest country in Asia. Her rise and fall are enough to shift everything in Asia. Therefore, to save Asia from decline, we must first start with the transformation of China, awaken the national consciousness of the people, and plan to build a great country with equality among five ethnic groups. This is a fact that everyone should acknowledge.

Based on this point, the birth of Asia began with research on the terrain, culture, politics, economy... of various Asian countries, past and present conditions, which is indeed something to be congratulated. The publication has now been published to Volume 2, Issue 1. Because it is a special oversized issue, articles on Asia - especially on the Chinese borderlands - are particularly abundant. They include Dai Jitao's general solution to the three problems of the Northeast, Northwest, and Southwest; Wei Chongyang's translation of The Precarious Manchurian-Mongolian Railway; Ma Quetian's A Glimpse of Outer Mongolia; Yu Quji's Cultivation of Wasteland in Xinjiang and Future Plans; Yang Zhonghua's Overview of Xikang; Zhang Fuzhen's Yunnan under French Imperialist Aggression; Li Shaoyun's Opening of Zhongshan Port and the Future of Southern China; Hua Qihua's The Topography of Eastern Nationalities and Their Revolutionary Movements; Chen Liepu's The Chinese National Movement on the International Stage of the Far East; Luo Jincheng's The Overseas Development of the Chinese Nation in the Past Century; Fang Baohan's India after the Round Table Conference; Wei Juezhong's The Scholars of the South Seas Dimuli Lilli under the Oppression of the Portuguese; Guo Shizhen's An Overview of Taiwan's Industry under the Power of Japanese Capital; and Chen Dazhong's Industry in Siberia, a total of fourteen articles, totaling more than 200,000 words. After reading it, I really gained a lot of knowledge. The essentials are introduced as follows:

(1) The Precarious Manchurian-Mongolian Railway

The Manchurian-Mongolian Railway is the most important business run by Japan to invade my Northeast, and it is also the general hub of economic power that Japan has grasped in the Northeast. Since its construction, it has dominated my Northeast for the past twenty-five years, and its business has been extremely prosperous, known as the "Manchurian Railway King." However, since the spring of last year, the situation has suddenly changed, and income has decreased, which is unprecedented. It is estimated that from April to August of last year

Page 22

At the end of the month, the railway revenue decreased by about 30 million yuan. Japan, which regards the Manchurian Railway as the life of the empire, discovered such a serious regression, so the government and the public were in turmoil, and the whole country was frenzied, seeking ways to provide relief. The author of this article, Tatsubun Takeuchi, was one of those sent to the Northeast by the Japanese government to investigate. Because of this, his remarks are very representative of the ambition of the entire Japanese imperialism to invade my Northeast. His design is to penetrate deep into the heart of my Northeast, which is worthy of our attention.

He analyzes the reasons why the revenue of the Manchurian Railway has decreased: 1. Due to the sharp drop in the price of silver; 2. China has made a planned resistance. Based on these reasons, he thought of a way to deal with it, which is quite alarming to us.

The Northeast was originally our country's territory. Because it could not withstand the oppression of Japan, it was just planning to build a railway to resist foreigners, but it was opposed by the Japanese. Isn't this the same as having your own things snatched away by a robber, and not even being allowed to say a word? Although the author does not agree with the "rescue, resort to the final means as soon as possible" of the Japanese residents who advocate war to treat me, he advocates "seeking a way for China and Japan to cooperate with each other in the railway, and discovering opportunities for diplomatic solutions." This is a policy that our people should pay attention to. The translation of this article in this publication has to be said to be an important thesis.

(2) A Glimpse of Outer Mongolia

The author of this article has traveled to Mongolia for a long time, so what he says is of course true. The full text is divided into three paragraphs. First, an overview of Outer Mongolia's finances is divided into one, customs duties; two, progressive property taxes; three, population donations and occupational donations; four, business donations and stamp duties; five, carriage and horse donations and rent donations; six, banking currency system, which describes the financial income of Outer Mongolia in great detail. The second paragraph describes the oppression of Han people in the mouths of Han merchants, just like heavy taxes, arbitrary fines, arbitrary interference, abuse, expulsion... all kinds of unequal treatment are really outrageous. The third paragraph, the attitude of the Han people towards the Three People's Principles, explains that ignorant Han merchants, because they indirectly received abuse from the Red Russians, suspected the Three People's Principles to be communism, and their stupidity is both pitiful and sighable. Usually, we always recognize Mongolia as our country's territory. However, judging from the facts stated in this article, Mongolia is simply like an enemy country to us.

(3) Yunnan under French Imperialist Aggression

From the perspective of Yunnan's position in national defense and international affairs, and the past and present social conditions, this article explains the ambition and attempt of French imperialists to invade. We indeed acknowledge that this article is an important thesis. In the introduction, the author tells us that Yunnan is the largest province in China, with an area of more than 107,900 square miles, fertile land, mild climate, abundant nonferrous metals, and rich animal husbandry. It is truly the so-called "unique natural endowment." However, recently, due to wars, bandits, corrupt officials, and dirty officials... all kinds of man-made disasters have brought the people of Yunnan to the brink of despair. The invasion of French imperialists has made Yunnan a meat on the chopping board and a fish in the cauldron. If the people of Yunnan do not become strong themselves, and the government does not pay attention, it will not stop until Yunnan is sent into the hands of foreigners. Later, the author listed the facts of French imperialists invading Yunnan, such as (A) in terms of politics and economy, the Yunnan-Vietnam Railway Company is managed by French people, and the post and telecommunications are still inseparable from the control of French people. Banque de l'Indochine holds the general hub of finance in the province. In addition, there are more foreign firms and companies than can be counted. The most bizarre thing is the militarization of the Yunnan-Vietnam Road, the increase of French police on the road, and the storage of gunpowder at the station, which is unpredictable. (B) Population oppression, the migration of large numbers of Annam people, making Yunnan suffer from overpopulation. (C) Cultural aggression, the detectives of Catholic teachers, and the increase of schools that manufacture foreign slaves. (D) Territorial encroachment, encroaching on our land across the border... All of this is really unimaginable to us. Yunnan is nominally one of the eighteen provinces of China, but in reality, it is so oppressed by imperialism. The author later discussed the way for the people of Yunnan to save themselves, should support the central government, fully develop national consciousness, and specifically pointed out seven positive and negative measures. We acknowledge that they are very appropriate.

(4) The Chinese National Movement on the International Stage of the Far East

This is a treatise discussing the international political situation, explaining the relationship between the Chinese national movement on the international stage of the Far East. The first paragraph, National Movement and Diplomacy, points out the necessity of diplomacy in the national movement, and cites the independence of North America, the unification of Italy after 1849, and the unification of Germany by Bismarck, none of which were achieved without diplomacy. The second paragraph, Ninety Years of Passive Diplomacy, points out the failure of Chinese diplomacy in modern times. A. The Chinese diplomacy in the period from the Opium War to the Sino-Japanese War, its driving force was the result of the imperialists' demand for trade. B. The Sino-Japanese War to the Boxer Rebellion was the diplomacy during the period of imperialist military aggression. C. From the Boxer Rebellion to the European War, it was the diplomacy of investment and aggression by the powers. The third paragraph, The Policies of the Powers towards China and their Conflicts, analyzes in detail the facts and interests of imperialists such as Britain, Japan, the United States, and Russia towards China. Because of this, the author affirms the direction of Chinese diplomacy said in the fourth paragraph, which must take Japan as a hypothetical enemy, unite with the United States to reject Britain, be friendly with Germany to prevent France, and give sufficient reasons. We cannot but acknowledge that it is correct. The fifth paragraph, The Brewing of the Second World War and the Preparations that China Should Make, points out that China, for the sake of national survival, should mobilize the whole people for preparations during the Second World War, and recognize that war is beneficial to our nation. It is concise, to the point, and extremely correct.

(5) The Savages of the South Seas under Portuguese Oppression in East Timor

The author, Mr. Wei Juezhong, is a traveler who has traveled alone to the South Seas Islands for seven years and has written a book "The Peoples of the Southern Wilderness." The reporter has introduced it in this publication. This article, "The Savages of the South Seas under Portuguese Oppression in East Timor," is still his work when he traveled to the South Seas. First, it describes the topography and location of East Timor, which is one of the Lesser Sunda Islands, with a wide jurisdiction. The northeast, south, and east are all facing the sea. Secondly, it describes the political situation of the Portuguese administration of Dili, the political orders are not implemented, and the officials are corrupt. Finally, there is the life of the savages, who are good at riding horses and produce abundant coffee, which is concise and interesting.

In addition to these important treatises, this publication also has a column "Asian Garden," which, according to the editor, "specializes in publishing the customs and poems of various parts of Asia," with the intention of focusing on interest, so as to avoid readers feeling boring and tasteless. The works published in this issue, such as Ge Ran Zeren's Tribute from Nepal in the Past and Wei Juezhong's Anti-Prison Notes from the South Island, can all be based on this purpose.

Looking at the various treatises in this issue, they all aim to dedicate themselves to the revival of Asia and discuss various issues related to Asia, focusing on the attention to the Chinese borderlands and the discussion of Eastern ethnic groups. This is naturally because, as mentioned above, China is the largest country in Asia, and China's rise and fall can shift the entire Asian context. However, in the past, we have not found a publication that focuses specifically on the examination of such issues. Because of this, this publication is indeed worth recommending.

Finally, I hope that the editors and authors of this publication will continue to work tirelessly. I especially hope that all Asian ethnic groups - especially the Chinese people - will pay attention to various issues related to the survival of Asia, and rise up to implement the Asian Ethnic Congress and jointly shout -

The whole of Asia has been revived!

Athletics at Great China University 162

— Bu Han

In the past, Great China University's athletics were indeed relatively quiet, but since moving to the new campus in the autumn of the nineteenth year [of the Republic, i.e., 1930], it seems that the spirit has been invigorated. It was indeed regrettable that they narrowly missed winning the Group B championship in last winter's West Qing basketball tournament (because the championship was held during the winter vacation, and many players had returned home, so they had to make do with players from the second team, and although they were defeated by Shanghai University, the score difference was very small), but they were able to defeat the extremely fierce combined team of St. John's Middle School—the youth team—in the Shanghai basketball tournament's Group B championship, which was no small consolation. And the recent vigor seems to have the momentum of advancing a thousand miles a day. (It is said that Xi Xuemin and others in the youth team were originally famous players from St. John's in Shanghai, and Lin Zequn, Hou Youliang, etc. were also first-class players from the university department. Mr. Hou also represented the Chinese team at the Shanghai International Basketball Tournament last year.)

In short, when I think of Great China University's athletics, I only feel that it is full of vigor, and it seems worthwhile to publish something about how strong its future strength will be.

First Volleyball Team: Holding the ambition to swallow up the south of the Yangtze River, although they lost to Jiangwan University in the first round of the Shih Pao Cup by a very small margin, that was when they had just formed the team, and there were some regrettable issues with coordination, as evidenced by the many missed balls in that game. But consider the subsequent friendly matches against Jinan University, Jiaotong University, the Law and Politics Department, St. John's University, the Central Political School, and the Chih Tze School, all of which were won by 3-0. In short, the Great China University volleyball team is unrivaled by any other school in Shanghai today, except for Fudan University, and even Fudan University is just a matter of luck—why not meet today!—and the even distribution of talent in the Great China University team is even more rare. The saves of Zhu Anmin, Lin Rangsen, Zhou Xiongwei, and Guan Pan'an, the spikes of Wei Dingyi and Wei Zuohan, and the sets of Ren Jiexing, etc., are all rare talents. And especially Wei Dingyi's spikes are even more powerful, often making the enemy tremble with fear.

Second Tennis Team: The Great China University tennis team, which won the championship in its first year of participating in the Jiangnan University Sports Association, was indeed a surprise and gave the people of Shanghai a good impression. Last year (the second year of Great China University's joining Jiangnan University), they defeated Central University and Jiaotong University in a row by 4-1, but ultimately failed to win the championship in the final, which was very regrettable. In the morning, Shen Meizhen and Guo Pengnian won two singles matches in a row, but in the two doubles matches in the afternoon, they lost two games in a row due to uneven pairings. If Shen and Guo could have been paired up for doubles, then the championship would not have been difficult. In short, this was not a fault of the players, but a problem with the sports director's strategy. Let's not dwell on the past and see who will win the championship in the upcoming tournament.

Third Basketball Team: The abundance of basketball talent here can be said to be second to none in the south of the Yangtze River. In addition to the original "locomotive" Kang Yuefa, "iron gate" Hu Mingxin, veteran Zhao Jiabin (a famous long-range shooter, but he will lack practice in the coming year), and other six or seven players, there is also Ren Jiexing, who is good at both attack and defense, and recently they have added several fierce generals from the "cannon team" who defeated Chih Tze, Qingguang, and Zhenru, making their strength even a hundred times stronger. They are just about to test their mettle. Unfortunately, the generals in the Jiangnan University basketball tournament could not participate due to eligibility issues, but they were still able to defeat Jiaotong University, Central University, Guanghua University, and the Central Public School in a row, which shows their strength.

Fourth Women's Basketball Team: Although it is their first time forming a team, their rapid progress is surprising. The fact that they defeated Chih Tze by 2-4 the other day is just a minor matter. Looking at their quick passing and brave attacking on that day, they are worthy of being a strong rival to Jinan University in the future.

Fifth Track and Field Team: The team includes Fang Sixu and Hu Mingxin, who specialize in shot put, discus, and javelin; He Debao, who specializes in sprinting; Long Zexian and Hu Dingli, who specialize in long-distance running; Wu Jinqi, who specializes in high jump; Guan Jiachang, who specializes in hurdles; and Lu Weikun and Zheng Bilian in the women's team, totaling no less than thirty or forty people, who are indeed a strong force. In addition to many team members being strong athletes from the Baihong and Jiangnan teams, Mr. Long was also a representative of China in last year's Far East Games. In the recent long-distance race organized by the Municipal Education Bureau, Mr. Long unfortunately had just recovered from a recent illness, and his strength was inevitably weakened, but he was still able to win the top prize (third place), which is no easy feat.

Other teams, such as the baseball team, are also practicing diligently. The famous Ren Jiexing is certainly extraordinary, but the other talents have not been able to show their skills because they still lack formal practice.

In short, the strength of Great China University is truly worth celebrating, and the upcoming expedition to Nanjing and Suzhou for track and field events will surely give us a better impression. Strive on!

Chih Tze College Invites Wu Jingxiong to Lecture 163

— Ling Xiao

Since Mr. He Shizhen founded Chih Tze College, he has strived for progress. A new school building is currently being built on Shuidao Road, costing hundreds of thousands of yuan, and is expected to be completed before the summer vacation. Recently, Principal He specially invited Mr. Wu Jingxiong, a lecturer at Harvard University and Northwestern University in the United States, to come to the school every Thursday from 4:00 to 6:00 to give lectures on the following topics: (1) The Art of Law, (2) Recent Trends in Western Law, (3) The Dispute Between Legalists and Confucians, (4) The Moral Components in Our Country's Old Legal System, (5) Cosmic Philosophy in Our Country's Old Legal System, (6) Six Periods in the History of Criminal Law in Our Country, (7) The Logic of "That's Terrible" in Judicial Adjudication, (8) Law and Nation, (9) Law and Civil Rights, (10) Law and People's Livelihood, which will be completed in ten lectures. Before Mr. Wu arrived at the college, all senior students prepared paper and pens and waited in the auditorium. Soon, Principal He and Secretary He accompanied Mr. Wu to the auditorium, and the hall resounded with applause. After Principal He introduced him, Mr. Wu took the stage and began his lecture, which was extremely brilliant, and all listeners admired him greatly.

Development of the Jiangnan Bell Sound Society 164

The Jiangnan College Bell Sound Society took only two weeks from preparation to establishment, and its planning has already been completed. It is reported that the executive committee has recently begun work. It is said that the society has appointed Ling Xianwen, Liu Zhujing, and Meng Xinmin as standing committee members, Cao Hanfang as the head of the general affairs department, Shao Rongjiu as the deputy, Jiang Zixuan as the head of the research department, Peng Ming as the deputy, Gu Jiwu as the head of the publication department, and Jin Caiqiao as the deputy. They have also hired Luo Xiuyun, Ying Yao, Yan Jiahua, and others to serve as group leaders in various groups, and they will intensify their work from now on, planning to publish publications on academic research in the shortest possible time, and inviting famous scholars to give lectures, paying close attention to both natural sciences and social sciences.

One Morning 165

— Ke

"Tangyuan Xishi [Dumpling Beauty]", this is a very attractive name. Not only are the male students in the universities near her residence crazy about her, but even the female students want to take the opportunity to admire her praised round and beautiful dimples. I am one of them.

It was a Friday morning. I had eaten porridge and was standing by the window idly holding a teacup when Xiang, who was sitting across from me, suddenly said,

"Yu, let's go to Baoshan now and see Tangyuan Xishi." Her face was full of happy smiles.

"Okay, let's call Ying and go together." This interesting suggestion brought my soul back from its immersion in humor.

So the three of us walked towards that long, black, sandy road. Gray clouds densely covered the sky, and a sea breeze mixed with sand and dust hit our faces. At this time, although we all felt a bit cold, we weren't discouraged - just thinking of that smile - that smile that made people happy - and still bravely and enthusiastically moved forward.

"Oh, it's raining," Xiang said.

"Yes, I'm getting a little wet too," I said anxiously.

"Don't argue," Ying comforted us, "we're almost there, almost at the tangyuan shop. Let's hurry and run there to take shelter from the rain."

At this time, the rain was getting heavier and heavier. We ran silently and quickly on the road.

Not far after entering the city gate, Ying pointed to a black-doored house in front and said, "Here we are, that's Xishi's house."

"There's no one at the door, it's so quiet it doesn't look like a pastry shop."

"Are we in the wrong place?" I said doubtfully. "I really don't believe that the tangyuan shop that everyone is talking about is so deserted."

"It can't be wrong, I've been here before, it's definitely right," Ying said firmly.

We walked into the shop. A woman in her forties was standing in front of the table chopping meat. The smile we braved the wind and rain to find was not there, indeed not there. Our eyes, like mice looking for food, searched everywhere with eager light, in the room, in the courtyard...

We asked the woman tentatively, "Tangyuan, we're here to eat tangyuan."

"She took them out to sell, she just left," the woman replied.

"Then... is there any..." Xiang seemed about to say something else.

I tugged at her shoulder, "Let's go, people will be suspicious." Xiang glared at me and followed me out.

At this time, disappointment replaced our excitement when we came. We walked in the cold wind and rain with our heads down, without saying a word.

There was a pastry shop by the road, with steamed buns and noodles. Steam was rising from the pot.

We felt a little empty in our stomachs and were afraid of getting our clothes wet, so we walked into the shop and went upstairs. The window upstairs faced the street. For some reason, I felt like this place was like an inn in a martial arts novel, and I myself seemed like a hero. I tapped the plate twice with my bamboo chopsticks, and a waiter ran up. We ordered some pastries and ate slowly, looking at the sky from time to time.

"Look," Ying said as if she had discovered something, "the raindrops aren't sparse anymore, the sky is clearing up, oh my god, we still have hope!" She jumped up happily.

Indeed, the rain had stopped. The sun gradually emerged from the clouds, the clouds scattered, letting out the sun, letting out the blue sky.

The clear weather and hot food dispelled our hunger, cold, and fatigue. We walked out of the shop and walked towards the beach, skipping and jumping.

A slightly curved, narrow, white road, obliquely hidden under the shade of trees on both sides, led to a not-so-high earthen slope. Walking up the earthen slope, you could see the surging white waves. The water here seemed even grander than at Paotai Bay, with no visible boundaries, only a faint line, a line separating the sky and the water. The sailboats in the distance and the cloud shadows on the horizon seemed not to move, slowly disappearing at the end of the sky and the water.

There was a row of stone slabs by the sea, as smooth as marble. We sat on the stone, and the warm sunlight happily enveloped the surroundings. I sighed softly and said to Ying, "Haven't you seen Tangyuan Xishi before? How beautiful is she?"

"I have seen her, but it was an evening, she was very busy, she put down the tangyuan and walked away. She never showed her smiling face, nor did she look at me. Although her graceful outline is still deeply imprinted in my mind, alas, I, with my nearsighted eyes, didn't see her face clearly at all."

Ying continued, "I have a fellow villager who studies at Zhongxiao, and I heard him say that that evening, the students at Zhongxiao took her to play in the dormitory, and many people made a lot of noise and had fun."

These words stirred up Xiang's usual easily triggered complaints. She cursed angrily,

"Damn society, damn men, they use all kinds of methods—seduction and oppression—to create women on the streets at night who are painted with powder and have red eyes, selling their bodies. They exploit her flesh and blood and then abandon her withered bones. Alas, this net of sin is raised high towards innocent girls—Tangyuan Xishi—waiting for her to fall down. Alas, educated, equality-advocating, intellectuals, what, ......"

As she spoke, she stretched out her waist and gently lay down on the stone slab, covering her eyes with her hands.

The Chinese Harmonica Society Goes to the Capital 166

— Liang

In recent years, many Chinese people have become interested in the harmonica. The harmonica is a very simple and inexpensive instrument, and learning to play it is not as difficult and time-consuming as other instruments—this is indeed a major reason why everyone is interested in the harmonica.

In Shanghai, there are many harmonica societies, and the most noteworthy and prestigious among them is of course the Chinese Harmonica Society. Under the guidance of harmonica expert Wang Qingxun, it has given public performances several times and has also broadcasted several times on the radio, allowing the national public to appreciate the art of the harmonica.

This time, the National Assembly, which the whole country longed for and which Premier Sun Yat-sen advocated, opened in the capital on May 5. The preparatory office and the authorities invited the Chinese Harmonica Society to perform in the capital for the appreciation of representatives from all provinces and cities across the country.

The departure date is May 1. The fare has been approved by the authorities and is free of charge. They will return in about ten days. There, one night, they will hold a concert at Jinling University. The ticket price is one yuan, eight jiao, and four jiao. The proceeds from the ticket sales will be used to supplement travel expenses and other purposes.

Guidelines for Youth Garden Contributions 167

(1) The content of the text should be related to discussions on youth issues, news about domestic and foreign schools or students, essays, descriptions of school life, and literary works. Editing will be discretionary.

(2) Illustrations should be limited to those related to youth issues.

(3) Photographs related to youth life (such as sports, travel, excursions, drama performances, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements are considered qualified. Individual or group photos are welcome.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(5) The number of words in each article should not exceed 2,000.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, and do not write in cursive. Western text should be omitted if possible, and if it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the Chinese text.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw illustrations, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black ink.

(8) Please specify that submissions should be sent to the Youth Garden Editorial Department.

(9) Please specify that submissions should be sent to the Women's Life Editorial Department.
